<p><b>Azerbaijan</b> (<span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/aɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>, <wbr />-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ʒ/: &#39;s&#39; in &#39;pleasure&#39;">ʒ</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Azerbaijan-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d8/En-Azerbaijan-pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="En-Azerbaijan-pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">US</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span><span title="/ər/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">ər</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/aɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">aɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>, <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;z&#39; in &#39;zoom&#39;">z</span></span>-/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>: <i lang="az">Azərbaycan</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Azerbaijani" title="Help:IPA/Azerbaijani">[ɑːzæɾbɑjˈd͡ʒɑn]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Azerbaijan</b> (<a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>: <i lang="az">Azərbaycan Respublikası</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Azerbaijani" title="Help:IPA/Azerbaijani">[ɑːzæɾbɑjˈd͡ʒɑn ɾespublikɑˈsɯ]</a></span>), is a country in the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">South Caucasus</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> at the crossroads of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It is bounded by the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> to the west and <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> to the south. The <a href="/wiki/Exclave" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclave">exclave</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic" title="Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic">Nakhchivan</a> is bounded by Armenia to the north and east, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> to the south and west, and has an 11&#160;km (6.8&#160;mi) long border with <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> in the northwest.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a> proclaimed its independence in 1918 and became the first secular democratic Muslim-majority state. In 1920 the country was incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic">Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Swietochowski_Borderland_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swietochowski_Borderland-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The modern Republic of Azerbaijan proclaimed its independence on 30 August 1991,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> shortly before the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the USSR</a> in the same year. In September 1991, the Armenian majority of the disputed <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a> region seceded to form the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Republic of Artsakh">Republic of Artsakh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The region and <a href="/wiki/Armenian-controlled_territories_surrounding_Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Armenian-controlled territories surrounding Nagorno-Karabakh">seven adjacent districts outside it</a> became <i>de facto</i> independent with the end of the <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="Nagorno-Karabakh War">Nagorno-Karabakh War</a> in 1994. These regions are internationally recognized as part of Azerbaijan pending a solution to the status of the Nagorno-Karabakh through negotiations facilitated by the <a href="/wiki/OSCE" class="mw-redirect" title="OSCE">OSCE</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Azerbaijan is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a><sup id="cite_ref-LaPorte2016_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaPorte2016-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>. It is one of six independent <a href="/wiki/List_of_Turkic_dynasties_and_countries#Current_independent_states" title="List of Turkic dynasties and countries">Turkic states</a> and an active member of the <a href="/wiki/Turkic_Council" title="Turkic Council">Turkic Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_of_Turkic_Culture" title="International Organization of Turkic Culture">TÜRKSOY</a> community. Azerbaijan has diplomatic relations with 158 countries and holds membership in 38 international organizations,<sup id="cite_ref-FCO_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCO-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> (since 1992), the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> (PfP) program. It is one of the founding members of <a href="/wiki/GUAM_Organization_for_Democracy_and_Economic_Development" title="GUAM Organization for Democracy and Economic Development">GUAM</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS)<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_the_Prohibition_of_Chemical_Weapons" title="Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons">Organisation for the Prohibition of Chemical Weapons</a>. Azerbaijan also holds observer status in the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FCO_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCO-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While more than 89% of the population is <a href="/wiki/Shia_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia Muslim">Shia Muslim</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Azerbaijan" title="Constitution of Azerbaijan">Constitution of Azerbaijan</a> does not declare an official religion and all major political forces in the country are <a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">secularist</a>. Azerbaijan has a high level of <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">human development</a> that ranks on par with most Eastern European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> It has a high rate of <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> as well as a low rate of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_unemployment_rate" title="List of countries by unemployment rate">unemployment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> However, the ruling party, the <a href="/wiki/New_Azerbaijan_Party" title="New Azerbaijan Party">New Azerbaijan Party</a>, has been accused of authoritarianism and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Azerbaijan" title="Human rights in Azerbaijan">human rights abuses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Atropatene" title="Atropatene">Atropatene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Albania" title="Caucasian Albania">Caucasian Albania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aran_to_Azerbaijan_name_change" class="mw-redirect" title="Aran to Azerbaijan name change">Aran to Azerbaijan name change</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbaijan_Republic_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Azerbaijan_Republic_map.png/220px-Azerbaijan_Republic_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e9/Azerbaijan_Republic_map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="328" data-file-height="339" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbaijan_Republic_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Azerbaijan and its main cities</div></div></div>
<p>According to a modern etymology, the term <i>Azerbaijan</i> derives from that of <i><a href="/wiki/Atropates" title="Atropates">Atropates</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schippmann_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schippmann-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian people">Persian</a><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Satrap" title="Satrap">satrap</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>, who was later reinstated as the satrap of <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Media</a> under <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chaumont_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chaumont-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dictionary_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictionary-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The original etymology of this name is thought to have its roots in the once-dominant <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Avesta" title="Avesta">Avesta</a>'s <i>Frawardin <a href="/wiki/Yasht" title="Yasht">Yasht</a></i> ("Hymn to the Guardian Angels"), there is a mention of <i>âterepâtahe ashaonô fravashîm ýazamaide</i>, which literally translates from <a href="/wiki/Avestan" title="Avestan">Avestan</a> as "we worship the <a href="/wiki/Fravashi" title="Fravashi">fravashi</a> of the holy <a href="/wiki/Atropatene" title="Atropatene">Atropatene</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The name "Atropates" itself is the Greek transliteration of an Old Iranian, probably <a href="/wiki/Median_language" title="Median language">Median</a>, compounded name with the meaning "Protected by the (Holy) Fire" or "The Land of the (Holy) Fire".<sup id="cite_ref-Library_of_Congress_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library_of_Congress-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The Greek name was mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Diodorus_Siculus" title="Diodorus Siculus">Diodorus Siculus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a>. Over the span of millennia, the name evolved to <i lang="pal-Latn" title="Middle Persian-language romanization">Āturpātākān</i> (<a href="/wiki/Middle_Persian" title="Middle Persian">Middle Persian</a>), then to <i lang="fa-Latn" title="Persian-language romanization">Ādharbādhagān</i>, <i lang="fa-Latn" title="Persian-language romanization">Ādharbāyagān</i>, <i lang="fa-Latn" title="Persian-language romanization">Āzarbāydjān</i> (New Persian) and present-day <i>Azerbaijan</i>.
</p><p>The name <i>Azerbaijan</i> was first adopted for the area of the present-day Republic of Azerbaijan by the government of <a href="/wiki/Musavat" title="Musavat">Musavat</a> in 1918,<sup id="cite_ref-Atabaki2006_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atabaki2006-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> after the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">collapse of the Russian Empire</a>, when the independent <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a> was established. Until then, the designation had been used exclusively to identify the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_(Iran)" title="Azerbaijan (Iran)">adjacent region of contemporary northwestern Iran</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-I.B.Tauris_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I.B.Tauris-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-I.B._Tauris_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I.B._Tauris-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Amsterdam_University_Press_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amsterdam_University_Press-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> while the area of the Azerbaijan Democratic Republic was formerly referred to as <i><a href="/wiki/Arran_(Caucasus)" title="Arran (Caucasus)">Arran</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Shirvan" title="Shirvan">Shirvan</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> On that basis Iran protested the newly adopted country name.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the Soviet rule, the country was also spelled in English from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_transliteration" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian transliteration">Russian transliteration</a> as <i>Azerbaydzhan</i> (<a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>&#58; <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">Азербайджа́н</span>).<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Azerbaijan" title="History of Azerbaijan">History of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Antiquity">Antiquity</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Albania" title="Caucasian Albania">Caucasian Albania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_Azerbaijan_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Ancient_Azerbaijan_4.jpg/220px-Ancient_Azerbaijan_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Ancient_Azerbaijan_4.jpg/330px-Ancient_Azerbaijan_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Ancient_Azerbaijan_4.jpg/440px-Ancient_Azerbaijan_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ancient_Azerbaijan_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Petroglyph" title="Petroglyph">Petroglyphs</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gobustan_National_Park" title="Gobustan National Park">Gobustan National Park</a> dating back to the <a href="/wiki/10th_millennium_BC" title="10th millennium BC">10th millennium BC</a> indicating a thriving culture. It is a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> considered to be of "outstanding universal value".</div></div></div>
<p>The earliest evidence of human settlement in the territory of Azerbaijan dates back to the late <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> and is related to the <a href="/wiki/Guruchay_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Guruchay culture">Guruchay culture</a> of <a href="/wiki/Azokh_Cave" title="Azokh Cave">Azokh Cave</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic" title="Upper Paleolithic">Upper Paleolithic</a> and late <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> cultures are attested in the caves of <a href="/wiki/Ta%C4%9F%C4%B1lar" title="Tağılar">Tağılar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damc%C4%B1l%C4%B1" title="Damcılı">Damcılı</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zar,_Azerbaijan" title="Zar, Azerbaijan">Zar</a>, Yataq-yeri and in the <a href="/wiki/Necropolis" title="Necropolis">necropolises</a> of Leylatepe and Saraytepe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Early settlements included the <a href="/wiki/Scythia" title="Scythia">Scythians</a> in the 9th century BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Library_of_Congress_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library_of_Congress-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Following the Scythians, Iranian <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Medes</a> came to dominate the area to the south of the <a href="/wiki/Aras_(river)" title="Aras (river)">Aras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dictionary_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dictionary-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The Medes forged a vast empire between 900–700&#160;BC, which was integrated into the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a> around 550&#160;BC.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The area was conquered by the Achaemenids leading to the spread of <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Later it became part of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(ancient_kingdom)" title="Macedonia (ancient kingdom)">Empire</a> and its successor, the <a href="/wiki/Seleucid_Empire" title="Seleucid Empire">Seleucid Empire</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> During this period, Zoroastrianism spread in the Caucasus and Atropatene. <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Albania" title="Caucasian Albania">Caucasian Albanians</a>, the original inhabitants of northeastern Azerbaijan,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> ruled that area from around the 4th century BC, and established an independent kingdom.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_the_Sasanid_period_to_the_Safavid_period">From the Sasanid period to the Safavid period</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:353px;max-width:353px"><div class="trow"><div class="theader" style="text-align:center;background-color:transparent">The <a href="/wiki/Maiden_Tower_(Baku)" title="Maiden Tower (Baku)">Maiden Tower</a> and The <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Shirvanshahs" title="Palace of the Shirvanshahs">Palace of the Shirvanshahs</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Old_City_(Baku)" title="Old City (Baku)">Old City</a> of Baku is a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> built in the 11th–12th century.</div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:162px;max-width:162px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Q%C4%B1z_qalas%C4%B1_%C3%BCmumi_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Maiden Tower" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Q%C4%B1z_qalas%C4%B1_%C3%BCmumi_2016.jpg/160px-Q%C4%B1z_qalas%C4%B1_%C3%BCmumi_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="160" height="126" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Q%C4%B1z_qalas%C4%B1_%C3%BCmumi_2016.jpg/240px-Q%C4%B1z_qalas%C4%B1_%C3%BCmumi_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Q%C4%B1z_qalas%C4%B1_%C3%BCmumi_2016.jpg/320px-Q%C4%B1z_qalas%C4%B1_%C3%BCmumi_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4374" data-file-height="3456" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:187px;max-width:187px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:%C5%9Eirvan%C5%9Fahlar_saray_kompleksi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Palace of the Shirvanshahs" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/%C5%9Eirvan%C5%9Fahlar_saray_kompleksi.jpg/185px-%C5%9Eirvan%C5%9Fahlar_saray_kompleksi.jpg" decoding="async" width="185" height="127" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/%C5%9Eirvan%C5%9Fahlar_saray_kompleksi.jpg/278px-%C5%9Eirvan%C5%9Fahlar_saray_kompleksi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/%C5%9Eirvan%C5%9Fahlar_saray_kompleksi.jpg/370px-%C5%9Eirvan%C5%9Fahlar_saray_kompleksi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5035" data-file-height="3456" /></a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empire</a> turned <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Albania" title="Caucasian Albania">Caucasian Albania</a> into a <a href="/wiki/Vassal_state" title="Vassal state">vassal state</a> in 252, while King <a href="/wiki/Urnayr" title="Urnayr">Urnayr</a> officially adopted <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> as the state religion in the 4th century<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. Despite Sassanid rule, <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Albania" title="Caucasian Albania">Albania</a> remained an entity in the region until the 9th century, while fully subordinate to Sassanid Iran, and retained its monarchy. Despite being one of the chief vassals of the Sasanian emperor, the Albanian king had only a semblance of authority, and the Sasanian <a href="/wiki/Marzban" title="Marzban">marzban</a> (military governor) held most civil, religious, and military authority.
</p><p>In the first half of the 7th century, <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Albania" title="Caucasian Albania">Caucasian Albania</a>, as a vassal of the Sasanians, came under nominal Muslim rule due to the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia" title="Muslim conquest of Persia">Muslim conquest of Persia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a> repulsed both the Sasanians and <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a> from <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a> and turned <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Albania" title="Caucasian Albania">Caucasian Albania</a> into a vassal state after Christian resistance led by King <a href="/wiki/Javanshir" title="Javanshir">Javanshir</a>, was suppressed in 667. The power vacuum left by the decline of the <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasid Caliphate</a> was filled by numerous local dynasties such as the <a href="/wiki/Sallarid_dynasty" title="Sallarid dynasty">Sallarids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sajid_dynasty" title="Sajid dynasty">Sajids</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shaddadids" title="Shaddadids">Shaddadids</a>. At the beginning of the 11th century, the territory was gradually seized by waves of <a href="/wiki/Oghuz_Turks" title="Oghuz Turks">Oghuz Turks</a> from <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>. The first of these Turkic dynasties established was the <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_Empire" title="Seljuk Empire">Seljuk Empire</a>, who entered the area now known as Azerbaijan by 1067.
</p><p>The pre-Turkic population that lived on the territory of modern Azerbaijan spoke several <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> and Caucasian languages, among them <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-VII_в_1877_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VII_в_1877-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> and an <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">Iranian language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Old_Azeri_language" title="Old Azeri language">Old Azeri</a>, which was gradually replaced by a <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic language</a>, the early precursor of the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani language</a> of today.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Some linguists have also stated that the <a href="/wiki/Tat_language_(Caucasus)" title="Tat language (Caucasus)">Tati dialects</a> of <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_(Iran)" title="Azerbaijan (Iran)">Iranian Azerbaijan</a> and the Republic of Azerbaijan, like those spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Tat_people_(Caucasus)" title="Tat people (Caucasus)">Tats</a>, are descended from Old Azeri.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Locally, the possessions of the subsequent Seljuk Empire were ruled by <a href="/wiki/Eldiguzids" title="Eldiguzids">Eldiguzids</a>, technically vassals of the Seljuk sultans, but sometimes <i>de facto</i> rulers themselves. Under the Seljuks, local poets such as <a href="/wiki/Nizami_Ganjavi" title="Nizami Ganjavi">Nizami Ganjavi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khaqani" title="Khaqani">Khaqani</a> gave rise to a blossoming of <a href="/wiki/Persian_literature" title="Persian literature">Persian literature</a> on the territory of present-day Azerbaijan.
</p><p>The local dynasty of the <a href="/wiki/Shirvanshah" title="Shirvanshah">Shirvanshahs</a> became a <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassal</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Timurid_dynasty" title="Timurid dynasty">Timur's Empire</a>, and assisted him in his war with the ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> <a href="/wiki/Tokhtamysh" title="Tokhtamysh">Tokhtamysh</a>. Following Timur's death, two independent and rival states emerged: <a href="/wiki/Kara_Koyunlu" title="Kara Koyunlu">Kara Koyunlu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aq_Qoyunlu" title="Aq Qoyunlu">Aq Qoyunlu</a>. The Shirvanshahs returned, maintaining a high degree of autonomy as local rulers and vassals from 861, for numerous centuries to come. In 1501, the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid dynasty</a> of Iran subdued the Shirvanshahs, and gained its possessions. In the course of the next century, the Safavids <a href="/wiki/Safavid_conversion_of_Iran_to_Shia_Islam" title="Safavid conversion of Iran to Shia Islam">converted the formerly Sunni population to Shia Islam</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> as they did with the population in what is modern-day Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The Safavids allowed the Shirvanshahs to remain in power, under Safavid suzerainty, until 1538, when Safavid king <a href="/wiki/Tahmasp_I" title="Tahmasp I">Tahmasp I</a> (r. 1524–1576) completely deposed them, and made the area into the Safavid province of <a href="/wiki/Safavid_Shirvan" title="Safavid Shirvan">Shirvan</a>. The Sunni Ottomans briefly managed to occupy parts of present-day Azerbaijan as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman-Safavid_War_(1578-1590)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman-Safavid War (1578-1590)">Ottoman-Safavid War of 1578–1590</a>; by the early 17th century, they were ousted by Safavid Iranian ruler <a href="/wiki/Abbas_I_of_Persia" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbas I of Persia">Abbas I</a> (r. 1588–1629). In the wake of the demise of the Safavid Empire, Baku and its environs were briefly occupied by the Russians as a consequence of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1722%E2%80%9323)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Persian War (1722–23)">Russo-Persian War of 1722–1723</a>. Despite brief intermissions such as these by Safavid Iran's neighboring rivals, the land of what is today Azerbaijan remained under Iranian rule from the earliest advent of the Safavids up to the course of the 19th century.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_history">Contemporary history</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_Wars" title="Russo-Persian Wars">Russo-Persian Wars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan" title="Treaty of Gulistan">Treaty of Gulistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Turkmenchay" title="Treaty of Turkmenchay">Treaty of Turkmenchay</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijan SSR">Azerbaijan SSR</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Edelweiss" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Edelweiss">Operation Edelweiss</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbaijani_khanates_in_the_18th-19th_centuries.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Azerbaijani_khanates_in_the_18th-19th_centuries.png/310px-Azerbaijani_khanates_in_the_18th-19th_centuries.png" decoding="async" width="310" height="416" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Azerbaijani_khanates_in_the_18th-19th_centuries.png/465px-Azerbaijani_khanates_in_the_18th-19th_centuries.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Azerbaijani_khanates_in_the_18th-19th_centuries.png/620px-Azerbaijani_khanates_in_the_18th-19th_centuries.png 2x" data-file-width="1093" data-file-height="1466" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbaijani_khanates_in_the_18th-19th_centuries.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Territories of the khanates (and sultanates) in the 18th–19th century</div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Safavid" class="mw-redirect" title="Safavid">Safavids</a>, the area was ruled by the Iranian <a href="/wiki/Afsharid_dynasty" title="Afsharid dynasty">Afsharid dynasty</a>. After the death of <a href="/wiki/Nader_Shah" title="Nader Shah">Nader Shah</a> (r. 1736–1747), many of his former subjects capitalized on the eruption of instability. Numerous self-ruling <a href="/wiki/Khanates_of_the_Caucasus" title="Khanates of the Caucasus">khanates</a> with various forms of autonomy<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> emerged in the area. The rulers of these khanates were directly related to the ruling dynasties of Iran, and were <a href="/wiki/Vassals" class="mw-redirect" title="Vassals">vassals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commoners" class="mw-redirect" title="Commoners">subjects</a> of the Iranian shah.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The khanates exercised control over their affairs via international trade routes between Central Asia and the West.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Thereafter, the area was under the successive rule of the Iranian <a href="/wiki/Zand_dynasty" title="Zand dynasty">Zands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> From the late 18th century, Imperial Russia switched to a more aggressive geo-political stance towards its two neighbors and rivals to the south, namely Iran and the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Russia now actively tried to gain possession of the Caucasus region which was, for the most part, in the hands of Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-CAUCAIRANICA_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAUCAIRANICA-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In 1804, the Russians <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ganja_(1804)" title="Battle of Ganja (1804)">invaded and sacked the Iranian town of Ganja</a>, sparking the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1804%E2%80%9313)" title="Russo-Persian War (1804–13)">Russo-Persian War of 1804–1813</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The militarily superior Russians ended the Russo-Persian War of 1804–1813 with a victory.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D0%B7%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D1%88%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/%D0%92%D0%B7%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D1%88%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8.jpg/170px-%D0%92%D0%B7%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D1%88%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/%D0%92%D0%B7%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D1%88%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8.jpg/255px-%D0%92%D0%B7%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D1%88%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/%D0%92%D0%B7%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D1%88%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8.jpg/340px-%D0%92%D0%B7%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D1%88%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3992" data-file-height="5524" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D0%B7%D1%8F%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%B8_%D1%88%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%BE%D0%BC_%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%BF%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B8.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ganja_(1804)" title="Battle of Ganja (1804)">The siege of Ganja Fortress in 1804</a> during the Russo-Persian War of 1804–1813 by Russian forces under the leadership of General <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Tsitsianov" title="Pavel Tsitsianov">Pavel Tsitsianov</a></div></div></div>
<p>Following Qajar Iran's loss in the 1804–1813 war, it was forced to concede suzerainty over most of the khanates, along with Georgia and Dagestan to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, per the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan" title="Treaty of Gulistan">Treaty of Gulistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The area to the north of the river <a href="/wiki/Aras_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Aras River">Aras</a>, amongst which territory lies the contemporary Republic of Azerbaijan, was Iranian territory until it was occupied by Russia in the 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Swietochowski_Borderland_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swietochowski_Borderland-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> About a decade later, in violation of the Gulistan treaty, the Russians invaded Iran's <a href="/wiki/Erivan_Khanate" title="Erivan Khanate">Erivan Khanate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> This sparked the final bout of hostilities between the two, the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_War_(1826-1828)" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Persian War (1826-1828)">Russo-Persian War of 1826–1828</a>. The resulting <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Turkmenchay" title="Treaty of Turkmenchay">Treaty of Turkmenchay</a>, forced <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar Iran</a> to cede sovereignty over the Erivan Khanate, the <a href="/wiki/Nakhchivan_Khanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Nakhchivan Khanate">Nakhchivan Khanate</a> and the remainder of the <a href="/wiki/Lankaran_Khanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Lankaran Khanate">Lankaran Khanate</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.nl_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.nl-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> comprising the last parts of the soil of the contemporary Azerbaijani Republic that were still in Iranian hands. After incorporation of all Caucasian territories from Iran into Russia, the new border between the two was set at the <a href="/wiki/Aras_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Aras River">Aras River</a>, which, upon the Soviet Union's disintegration, subsequently became part of the border between Iran and the Azerbaijan Republic.
</p><p>Qajar Iran was forced to cede its Caucasian territories to Russia in the 19th century, which thus included the territory of the modern-day Azerbaijan Republic, while as a result of that cession, the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijani ethnic group</a> is nowadays parted between two nations: Iran and Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Nevertheless, the number of ethnic Azerbaijanis in Iran far outnumber those in neighbouring Azerbaijan.
</p><p>After the collapse of the Russian Empire during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasian_Democratic_Federative_Republic" title="Transcaucasian Democratic Federative Republic">Transcaucasian Democratic Federative Republic</a> was declared, constituting the present-day republics of Azerbaijan, Georgia, and Armenia.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_iran_azerbaijan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Ottoman_iran_azerbaijan.jpg/220px-Ottoman_iran_azerbaijan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Ottoman_iran_azerbaijan.jpg/330px-Ottoman_iran_azerbaijan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Ottoman_iran_azerbaijan.jpg/440px-Ottoman_iran_azerbaijan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="835" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ottoman_iran_azerbaijan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iran's official protest, after adoption of the name of Azerbaijan in 1918: "Naming the recently-created state of Caucasus "Azerbaijan", which was created in the aftermath of your (Ottomans) peace with Russia, while there is a province in Iran with the same name, surprised us. The embassy [of Iran] thinks a reconsideration is necessary."</div></div></div>
<p>It was followed by the <a href="/wiki/March_Days" title="March Days">March Days</a> massacres<sup id="cite_ref-smithmusavat_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smithmusavat-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-minahan_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minahan-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> that took place between 30 March and 2 April 1918 in the city of <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> and adjacent areas of the <a href="/wiki/Baku_Governorate" title="Baku Governorate">Baku Governorate</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> When the republic dissolved in May 1918, the leading <a href="/wiki/Musavat" title="Musavat">Musavat</a> party declared independence as the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a> (ADR), adopting the name of "Azerbaijan" for the new republic; a name that prior to the proclamation of the ADR was solely used to refer to the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Iranian Azerbaijan">northwestern region of contemporary Iran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-I.B.Tauris_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I.B.Tauris-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-I.B._Tauris_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-I.B._Tauris-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Amsterdam_University_Press_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amsterdam_University_Press-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The ADR was the first modern <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a> in the Muslim world.<sup id="cite_ref-Swietochowski_Borderland_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swietochowski_Borderland-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kazemzadeh_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kazemzadeh-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Among the important accomplishments of the Parliament was the extension of suffrage to women, making Azerbaijan the first Muslim nation to grant women equal political rights with men.<sup id="cite_ref-kazemzadeh_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kazemzadeh-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Another important accomplishment of ADR was the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Baku_State_University" title="Baku State University">Baku State University</a>, which was the first modern-type university founded in the Muslim East.<sup id="cite_ref-kazemzadeh_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kazemzadeh-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1ST_AZ_REP.GIF" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/1ST_AZ_REP.GIF/330px-1ST_AZ_REP.GIF" decoding="async" width="330" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/1ST_AZ_REP.GIF/495px-1ST_AZ_REP.GIF 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/1ST_AZ_REP.GIF/660px-1ST_AZ_REP.GIF 2x" data-file-width="1976" data-file-height="1387" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1ST_AZ_REP.GIF" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map presented by the delegation of Azerbaijan in the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">1919 Paris Peace Conference</a></div></div></div><p> By March 1920, it was obvious that Soviet Russia would attack Baku. <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> said that the invasion was justified as <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Soviet Russia</a> could not survive without Baku's <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Azerbaijan" title="Petroleum industry in Azerbaijan">oil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Independent Azerbaijan lasted only 23 months until the <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> <a href="/wiki/11th_Soviet_Red_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="11th Soviet Red Army">11th Soviet Red Army</a> invaded it, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic">Azerbaijan SSR</a> on 28 April 1920. Although the bulk of the newly formed Azerbaijani army was engaged in putting down an Armenian revolt that had just broken out in <a href="/wiki/Karabakh" title="Karabakh">Karabakh</a>, Azerbaijanis did not surrender their brief independence of 1918–20 quickly or easily. As many as 20,000 Azerbaijani soldiers died resisting what was effectively a Russian reconquest.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 13 October 1921, the Soviet republics of Russia, Armenia, Azerbaijan, and Georgia signed an agreement with Turkey known as the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kars" title="Treaty of Kars">Treaty of Kars</a>. The previously independent <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Aras" title="Republic of Aras">Republic of Aras</a> would also become the <a href="/wiki/Nakhichevan_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Nakhichevan Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Nakhichevan Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> within the Azerbaijan SSR by the treaty of Kars. On the other hand, <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> was awarded the region of <a href="/wiki/Syunik_Province" title="Syunik Province">Zangezur</a> and Turkey agreed to return <a href="/wiki/Gyumri" title="Gyumri">Gyumri</a> (then known as Alexandropol).
</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Azerbaijan played a crucial role in the strategic energy policy of the Soviet Union, with 80 percent of the Soviet Union's oil on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a> being supplied by Baku. By the Decree of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_the_USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Soviet of the USSR">Supreme Soviet of the USSR</a> in February 1942, the commitment of more than 500 workers and employees of the <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry" title="Petroleum industry">oil industry</a> of Azerbaijan were awarded orders and medals. <a href="/wiki/Operation_Edelweiss" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Edelweiss">Operation Edelweiss</a> carried out by the German <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> targeted Baku because of its importance as the energy (petroleum) dynamo of the USSR.<sup id="cite_ref-Swietochowski_Borderland_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swietochowski_Borderland-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> A fifth of all Azerbaijanis fought in the Second World War from 1941 to 1945. Approximately 681,000 people with over 100,000 of them women went to the front, while the total population of Azerbaijan was 3.4&#160;million at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Some 250,000 people from Azerbaijan were killed on the front. More than 130 Azerbaijanis were named <a href="/wiki/Hero_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Hero of the Soviet Union">Heroes of the Soviet Union</a>. Azerbaijani Major-General <a href="/wiki/Azi_Aslanov" class="mw-redirect" title="Azi Aslanov">Azi Aslanov</a> was twice awarded the Hero of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RedArmy_Paratroops_Baku_1990.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/RedArmy_Paratroops_Baku_1990.jpg/220px-RedArmy_Paratroops_Baku_1990.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/RedArmy_Paratroops_Baku_1990.jpg/330px-RedArmy_Paratroops_Baku_1990.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/RedArmy_Paratroops_Baku_1990.jpg/440px-RedArmy_Paratroops_Baku_1990.jpg 2x" data-file-width="696" data-file-height="513" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RedArmy_Paratroops_Baku_1990.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> <a href="/wiki/Paratroops" class="mw-redirect" title="Paratroops">paratroops</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Black_January" title="Black January">Black January</a> tragedy in 1990</div></div></div>
<p>Following the politics of <i><a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">glasnost</a></i>, initiated by <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>, civil unrest and ethnic strife grew in various regions of the Soviet Union, including <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Croissant_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Croissant-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> an autonomous region of the Azerbaijan SSR. The disturbances in Azerbaijan, in response to Moscow's indifference to an already heated conflict, resulted in calls for independence and secession, which culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Black_January" title="Black January">Black January</a> events in Baku.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Later in 1990, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_Azerbaijan_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Soviet of Azerbaijan SSR">Supreme Council of the Azerbaijan SSR</a> dropped the words "Soviet Socialist" from the title, adopted the "Declaration of Sovereignty of the Azerbaijan Republic" and restored the flag of the Azerbaijan Democratic Republic as the state flag.<sup id="cite_ref-Meclis_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meclis-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> As a consequence of the <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d&#39;état attempt">failed coup which occurred in August in Moscow</a>, on 18 October 1991, the Supreme Council of Azerbaijan adopted a Declaration of Independence which was affirmed by a nationwide referendum in December 1991, while the Soviet Union officially ceased to exist on 26 December 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-Meclis_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meclis-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The country now celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Azerbaijan)" title="Independence Day (Azerbaijan)">Independence Day</a> on 18 October.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The early years of independence were overshadowed by the <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Nagorno-Karabakh war">Nagorno-Karabakh war</a> with the ethnic Armenian majority of Nagorno-Karabakh backed by Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the hostilities in 1994, Armenians controlled up to 20 percent of Azerbaijani territory, including Nagorno-Karabakh itself.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DeWaal_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeWaal-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> During the war many atrocities were committed including the <a href="/wiki/Massacre" title="Massacre">massacres</a> at <a href="/wiki/Malibeyli_and_Gushchular_Massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Malibeyli and Gushchular Massacre">Malibeyli and Gushchular</a>, the Garadaghly massacre, the Agdaban and the <a href="/wiki/Khojaly_massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Khojaly massacre">Khojaly massacres</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, an estimated 30,000 people have been killed and more than a million people have been displaced.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Four <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> Resolutions (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_822" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 822">822</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_853" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 853">853</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_874" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 874">874</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_884" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 884">884</a>) demand for "the immediate withdrawal of all Armenian forces from all occupied territories of Azerbaijan."<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Many Russians and Armenians left Azerbaijan during the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> According to the 1970 census, there were 510,000 ethnic <a href="/wiki/Russian_diaspora" title="Russian diaspora">Russians</a> and 484,000 Armenians in Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nagorno-Karabakh_Map2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nagorno-Karabakh_Map2.png/220px-Nagorno-Karabakh_Map2.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nagorno-Karabakh_Map2.png/330px-Nagorno-Karabakh_Map2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nagorno-Karabakh_Map2.png/440px-Nagorno-Karabakh_Map2.png 2x" data-file-width="1673" data-file-height="837" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nagorno-Karabakh_Map2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Current military situation in separatist <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1993, democratically elected president <a href="/wiki/Abulfaz_Elchibey" title="Abulfaz Elchibey">Abulfaz Elchibey</a> was overthrown by a military insurrection led by Colonel <a href="/wiki/Surat_Huseynov" title="Surat Huseynov">Surat Huseynov</a>, which resulted in the rise to power of the former leader of <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic">Soviet Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heydar_Aliyev" title="Heydar Aliyev">Heydar Aliyev</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In 1994, Surat Huseynov, by that time the prime minister, attempted another military coup against Heydar Aliyev, but he was arrested and charged with treason.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> A year later, in 1995, another <a href="/wiki/1995_Azerbaijani_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1995 Azerbaijani coup d&#39;état attempt">coup</a> was attempted against Aliyev, this time by the commander of the <a href="/wiki/OMON" title="OMON">OMON</a> special unit, <a href="/wiki/Rovshan_Javadov" title="Rovshan Javadov">Rovshan Javadov</a>. The coup was averted, resulting in the killing of the latter and disbanding of Azerbaijan's OMON units.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lt_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lt-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, the country was tainted by rampant corruption in the governing bureaucracy.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In October 1998, Aliyev was reelected for a second term. Despite the much improved economy, particularly with the exploitation of the <a href="/wiki/Azeri-Chirag-Guneshli" class="mw-redirect" title="Azeri-Chirag-Guneshli">Azeri-Chirag-Guneshli oil field</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shah_Deniz_gas_field" title="Shah Deniz gas field">Shah Deniz gas field</a>, Aliyev's presidency was criticized due to suspected election frauds and corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">Ilham Aliyev</a>, Heydar Aliyev's son, became chairman of the <a href="/wiki/New_Azerbaijan_Party" title="New Azerbaijan Party">New Azerbaijan Party</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/President_of_Azerbaijan" title="President of Azerbaijan">President</a> of Azerbaijan when his father died in 2003. He was <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_presidential_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani presidential election, 2013">reelected to a third term</a> as president in October 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_AZE_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Koppen-Geiger_Map_AZE_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_AZE_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Koppen-Geiger_Map_AZE_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_AZE_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Koppen-Geiger_Map_AZE_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_AZE_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1715" data-file-height="850" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_AZE_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen-Geiger climate classification</a> map for Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Azerbaijan" title="Geography of Azerbaijan">Geography of Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_Azerbaijan" title="Environment of Azerbaijan">Environment of Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_reserves_of_Azerbaijan" title="State reserves of Azerbaijan">State reserves of Azerbaijan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/National_parks_of_Azerbaijan" title="National parks of Azerbaijan">National parks of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Extreme_points_of_Azerbaijan" title="Extreme points of Azerbaijan">Extreme points of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Budug_Azerbaijan16.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Budug_Azerbaijan16.jpg/220px-Budug_Azerbaijan16.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Budug_Azerbaijan16.jpg/330px-Budug_Azerbaijan16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Budug_Azerbaijan16.jpg/440px-Budug_Azerbaijan16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1504" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Budug_Azerbaijan16.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> in northern Azerbaijan</div></div></div>
<p>Geographically, Azerbaijan is located in the <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus" class="mw-redirect" title="South Caucasus">South Caucasus</a> region of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, straddling <a href="/wiki/Southwest_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Southwest Asia">Western Asia</a> and Eastern Europe. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/38th_parallel_north" title="38th parallel north">38°</a> and <a href="/wiki/42nd_parallel_north" title="42nd parallel north">42° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/44th_meridian_east" title="44th meridian east">44°</a> and <a href="/wiki/51st_meridian_east" title="51st meridian east">51° E</a>. The total length of Azerbaijan's <a href="/wiki/List_of_land_border_lengths" class="mw-redirect" title="List of land border lengths">land borders</a> is 2,648&#160;km (1,645&#160;mi), of which 1,007&#160;kilometers are with Armenia, 756&#160;kilometers with Iran, 480&#160;kilometers with Georgia, 390&#160;kilometers with Russia and 15&#160;kilometers with Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-STA_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STA-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Coast" title="Coast">coastline</a> stretches for 800&#160;km (497&#160;mi), and the length of the widest area of the Azerbaijani section of the Caspian Sea is 456&#160;km (283&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-STA_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STA-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The territory of Azerbaijan extends 400&#160;km (249&#160;mi) from north to south, and 500&#160;km (311&#160;mi) from west to east.
</p><p>Three physical features dominate Azerbaijan: the Caspian Sea, whose shoreline forms a natural boundary to the east; the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Caucasus" title="Greater Caucasus">Greater Caucasus</a> mountain range to the north; and the extensive flatlands at the country's center. There are also three mountain ranges, the Greater and <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Caucasus" title="Lesser Caucasus">Lesser Caucasus</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Talysh_Mountains" title="Talysh Mountains">Talysh Mountains</a>, together covering approximately 40% of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-GEO_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEO-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The highest peak of Azerbaijan is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Bazard%C3%BCz%C3%BC" title="Mount Bazardüzü">Mount Bazardüzü</a> (4,466&#160;m), while the lowest point lies in the Caspian Sea (−28&#160;m). Nearly half of all the <a href="/wiki/Mud_volcano" title="Mud volcano">mud volcanoes</a> on Earth are concentrated in Azerbaijan, <a href="/wiki/Mud_volcanoes_in_Azerbaijan" title="Mud volcanoes in Azerbaijan">these volcanoes</a> were also among nominees for the <a href="/wiki/New7Wonders_of_Nature" title="New7Wonders of Nature">New7Wonders of Nature</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main water sources are surface waters. However, only 24 of the 8,350 rivers are greater than 100&#160;km (62&#160;mi) in length.<sup id="cite_ref-GEO_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEO-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> All the rivers drain into the Caspian Sea in the east of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-GEO_113-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEO-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The largest lake is <a href="/wiki/Lake_Sarysu" title="Lake Sarysu">Sarysu</a> (67&#160;km²), and the longest river is <a href="/wiki/Kura_(Caspian_Sea)" title="Kura (Caspian Sea)">Kur</a> (1,515&#160;km), which is <a href="/wiki/Transboundary_river" title="Transboundary river">transboundary</a> with <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>. Azerbaijan's four main islands in the Caspian Sea have a combined area of over thirty square kilometers.
</p><p>Since the independence of Azerbaijan in 1991, the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Azerbaijan" title="Politics of Azerbaijan">Azerbaijani government</a> has taken measures to preserve the environment of Azerbaijan. National protection of the environment accelerated after 2001 when the state budget increased due to new revenues provided by the <a href="/wiki/Baku-Tbilisi-Ceyhan_pipeline" class="mw-redirect" title="Baku-Tbilisi-Ceyhan pipeline">Baku-Tbilisi-Ceyhan pipeline</a>. Within four years protected areas doubled and now make up eight percent of the country's territory. Since 2001 the government has set up seven large reserves and almost doubled the sector of the budget earmarked for environmental protection.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landscape">Landscape</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Orography_of_Azerbaijan" title="Orography of Azerbaijan">Orography of Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Azerbaijan" title="Climate of Azerbaijan">Climate of Azerbaijan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Water_bodies_of_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Water bodies of Azerbaijan">Water bodies of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bazarduzu_detail.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Bazarduzu_detail.JPG/220px-Bazarduzu_detail.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Bazarduzu_detail.JPG/330px-Bazarduzu_detail.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Bazarduzu_detail.JPG/440px-Bazarduzu_detail.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bazarduzu_detail.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Bazard%C3%BCz%C3%BC" title="Mount Bazardüzü">Mount Bazarduzu</a>, the highest peak of Azerbaijan, as seen from <a href="/wiki/Mount_Shahdagh" title="Mount Shahdagh">Mount Shahdagh</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbajiani_landscape_-_Another_version.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Azerbajiani_landscape_-_Another_version.jpg/220px-Azerbajiani_landscape_-_Another_version.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Azerbajiani_landscape_-_Another_version.jpg/330px-Azerbajiani_landscape_-_Another_version.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Azerbajiani_landscape_-_Another_version.jpg/440px-Azerbajiani_landscape_-_Another_version.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2430" data-file-height="1370" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbajiani_landscape_-_Another_version.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The landscape of Khinalug valley</div></div></div>
<p>Azerbaijan is home to a vast variety of landscapes. Over half of Azerbaijan's land mass consists of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mountain_ridges&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mountain ridges (page does not exist)">mountain ridges</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_crest" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain crest">crests</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Yailas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Yailas (page does not exist)">yailas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Plateaus" class="mw-redirect" title="Plateaus">plateaus</a> which rise up to hypsometric levels of 400–1000&#160;meters (including the Middle and Lower lowlands), in some places (Talis, Jeyranchol-Ajinohur and Langabiz-Alat foreranges) up to 100–120&#160;meters, and others from 0–50&#160;meters and up (<a href="/wiki/Qobustan,_Absheron" title="Qobustan, Absheron">Qobustan, Absheron</a>). The rest of Azerbaijan's terrain consist of plains and lowlands. Hypsometric marks within the Caucasus region vary from about −28&#160;meters at the Caspian Sea shoreline up to 4,466&#160;meters (Bazardüzü peak).<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The formation of climate in Azerbaijan is influenced particularly by cold <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">arctic</a> <a href="/wiki/Air_mass" title="Air mass">air masses</a> of Scandinavian <a href="/wiki/Anticyclone" title="Anticyclone">anticyclone</a>, temperate air masses of <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberian</a> anticyclone, and Central Asian anticyclone.<sup id="cite_ref-CLIM_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CLIM-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijan's diverse landscape affects the ways air masses enter the country.<sup id="cite_ref-CLIM_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CLIM-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> The Greater Caucasus protects the country from direct influences of cold air masses coming from the north. That leads to the formation of <a href="/wiki/Subtropics" title="Subtropics">subtropical climate</a> on most foothills and plains of the country. Meanwhile, plains and foothills are characterized by high <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">solar radiation</a> rates.
</p><p>9 out of 11 existing <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">climate zones</a> are present in Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-KL_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KL-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Both the absolute minimum temperature (<span style="white-space:nowrap"> −33&#160;°C or −27.4&#160;°F </span>) and the absolute maximum temperature (<span style="white-space:nowrap"> 46&#160;°C or 114.8&#160;°F </span>) were observed in <a href="/wiki/Julfa_Rayon" class="mw-redirect" title="Julfa Rayon">Julfa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ordubad_Rayon" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordubad Rayon">Ordubad</a> – regions of <a href="/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic" title="Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic">Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KL_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KL-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The maximum annual <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">precipitation</a> falls in <a href="/wiki/Lankaran" title="Lankaran">Lankaran</a> (1,600 to 1,800&#160;mm or 63 to 71&#160;in) and the minimum in Absheron (200 to 350&#160;mm or 7.9 to 13.8&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-KL_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KL-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Murov_mountain_in_Azerbaijan-Caucasus3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Murov_mountain_in_Azerbaijan-Caucasus3.jpg/220px-Murov_mountain_in_Azerbaijan-Caucasus3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Murov_mountain_in_Azerbaijan-Caucasus3.jpg/330px-Murov_mountain_in_Azerbaijan-Caucasus3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Murov_mountain_in_Azerbaijan-Caucasus3.jpg/440px-Murov_mountain_in_Azerbaijan-Caucasus3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="513" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Murov_mountain_in_Azerbaijan-Caucasus3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Murovdag" title="Murovdag">Murovdag</a> is the highest <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">mountain range</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Caucasus" title="Lesser Caucasus">Lesser Caucasus</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Rivers and lakes form the principal part of the water systems of Azerbaijan, they were formed over a long geological timeframe and changed significantly throughout that period. This is particularly evidenced by remnants of ancient rivers found throughout the country. The country's water systems are continually changing under the influence of natural forces and human introduced industrial activities. Artificial rivers (canals) and ponds are a part of Azerbaijan's water systems. In terms of water supply, Azerbaijan is below the average in the world with approximately 100,000 cubic metres (3,531,467 cubic feet) per year of water per square kilometer.<sup id="cite_ref-KL_118-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KL-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> All big <a href="/wiki/Reservoir" title="Reservoir">water reservoirs</a> are built on Kur. The hydrography of Azerbaijan basically belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Caspian Sea basin">Caspian Sea basin</a>.
</p><p>There are 8,350 rivers of various lengths within Azerbaijan. Only 24 rivers are over 100&#160;kilometers long.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kura_(Caspian_Sea)" title="Kura (Caspian Sea)">Kura</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aras_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Aras River">Aras</a> are the major rivers in Azerbaijan, they run through the <a href="/wiki/Kura-Aras_Lowland" class="mw-redirect" title="Kura-Aras Lowland">Kura-Aras Lowland</a>. The rivers that directly flow into the Caspian Sea, originate mainly from the north-eastern slope of the Major Caucasus and <a href="/wiki/Talysh_Mountains" title="Talysh Mountains">Talysh Mountains</a> and run along the Samur–Devechi and Lankaran lowlands.
