</p><p><a href="/wiki/Yanar_Dag" title="Yanar Dag">Yanar Dag</a>, translated as "burning mountain", is a natural gas fire which blazes continuously on a hillside on the <a href="/wiki/Absheron_Peninsula" title="Absheron Peninsula">Absheron Peninsula</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a> near <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>, which itself is known as the "land of fire." Flames jet out into the air from a thin, porous sandstone layer. It is a tourist attraction to visitors to the Baku area.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Azerbaijan" title="Wildlife of Azerbaijan">Wildlife of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Fauna_of_Azerbaijan" title="Fauna of Azerbaijan">Fauna of Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flora_of_Azerbaijan" title="Flora of Azerbaijan">Flora of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stamps_of_Azerbaijan,_2006-750.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Stamps_of_Azerbaijan%2C_2006-750.jpg/220px-Stamps_of_Azerbaijan%2C_2006-750.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Stamps_of_Azerbaijan%2C_2006-750.jpg/330px-Stamps_of_Azerbaijan%2C_2006-750.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Stamps_of_Azerbaijan%2C_2006-750.jpg/440px-Stamps_of_Azerbaijan%2C_2006-750.jpg 2x" data-file-width="614" data-file-height="445" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stamps_of_Azerbaijan,_2006-750.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Karabakh_horse" title="Karabakh horse">Karabakh horse</a> is the national animal of Azerbaijan.</div></div></div>
<p>The first reports on the richness and diversity of animal life in Azerbaijan can be found in travel notes of Eastern travelers. Animal carvings on architectural monuments, ancient rocks and stones survived up to the present times. The first information on the flora and fauna of Azerbaijan was collected during the visits of naturalists to Azerbaijan in the 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-GEO_113-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEO-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are 106 species of mammals, 97 species of fish, 363 species of birds, 10 species of amphibians and 52 species of reptiles which have been recorded and classified in Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-GEO_113-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEO-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The national animal of Azerbaijan is the <a href="/wiki/Karabakh_horse" title="Karabakh horse">Karabakh horse</a>, a mountain-steppe racing and riding horse endemic to Azerbaijan. The Karabakh horse has a reputation for its good temper, speed, elegance and intelligence. It is one of the oldest breeds, with ancestry dating to the ancient world. However, today the horse is an endangered species.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Azerbaijan's flora consists of more than 4,500 species of <a href="/wiki/Higher_plants" class="mw-redirect" title="Higher plants">higher plants</a>. Due to the unique climate in Azerbaijan, the flora is much richer in the number of species than the flora of the other republics of the South Caucasus.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> About 67 percent of the species growing in the whole <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a> can be found in Azerbaijan.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Azerbaijan" title="Politics of Azerbaijan">Politics of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Azerbaijan" title="Elections in Azerbaijan">Elections in Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Azerbaijan" title="Human rights in Azerbaijan">Human rights in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gobierno_de_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n,_Baku,_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n,_2016-09-26,_DD_27.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Gobierno_de_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_Baku%2C_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_2016-09-26%2C_DD_27.jpg/220px-Gobierno_de_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_Baku%2C_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_2016-09-26%2C_DD_27.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Gobierno_de_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_Baku%2C_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_2016-09-26%2C_DD_27.jpg/330px-Gobierno_de_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_Baku%2C_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_2016-09-26%2C_DD_27.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Gobierno_de_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_Baku%2C_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_2016-09-26%2C_DD_27.jpg/440px-Gobierno_de_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_Baku%2C_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n%2C_2016-09-26%2C_DD_27.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8083" data-file-height="4132" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gobierno_de_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n,_Baku,_Azerbaiy%C3%A1n,_2016-09-26,_DD_27.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Government building in Baku</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Munich_Security_Conference_2010_-_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Munich_Security_Conference_2010_-_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg/170px-Munich_Security_Conference_2010_-_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Munich_Security_Conference_2010_-_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg/255px-Munich_Security_Conference_2010_-_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Munich_Security_Conference_2010_-_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg/340px-Munich_Security_Conference_2010_-_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2336" data-file-height="3504" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Munich_Security_Conference_2010_-_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The son of former President <a href="/wiki/Heydar_Aliyev" title="Heydar Aliyev">Heydar Aliyev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">Ilham Aliyev</a>, succeeded his father and has remained in power since 2003.</div></div></div>
<p>The structural formation of Azerbaijan's political system was completed by the adoption of the new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Azerbaijan" title="Constitution of Azerbaijan">Constitution</a> on 12 November 1995. According to Article 23 of the Constitution, the <a href="/wiki/National_symbol" title="National symbol">state symbols</a> of the Azerbaijan Republic are the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Azerbaijan" title="Flag of Azerbaijan">flag</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Coat of arms of Azerbaijan">coat of arms</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Anthem_of_the_Republic_of_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="National Anthem of the Republic of Azerbaijan">national anthem</a>. The state power in Azerbaijan is limited only by law for internal issues, but for international affairs is additionally limited by the provisions of international agreements.
</p><p>The Constitution of Azerbaijan states that it is a presidential republic with three branches of power – Executive, Legislative and Judicial. The legislative power is held by the <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Azerbaijan">National Assembly</a> and the Supreme National Assembly in the Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic. The Parliament of Azerbaijan, called Milli Majlis, consists of 125 deputies and elected based on majority voting system, with a term of 5 years for each elected member. The elections are held every five years, on the first Sunday of November. The Parliament is not responsible for formation of the government, but the Constitution requires approval of the Cabinet of Ministers by Milli Majlis<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/New_Azerbaijan_Party" title="New Azerbaijan Party">Yeni Azerbaijan Party</a>, and independents loyal to the ruling government, currently hold almost all of the Parliament's 125 seats. During the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_parliamentary_election,_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani parliamentary election, 2010">2010 Parliamentary election</a>, the opposition parties, <a href="/wiki/Musavat" title="Musavat">Musavat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_Popular_Front_Party" title="Azerbaijani Popular Front Party">Azerbaijani Popular Front Party</a>, failed to win a single seat. European observers <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_parliamentary_election,_2010#Campaign_irregularities" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani parliamentary election, 2010">found numerous irregularities</a> in the run-up to the election and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_parliamentary_election,_2010#Election" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani parliamentary election, 2010">on election day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The executive power is held by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Azerbaijan" title="President of Azerbaijan">President</a>, who is elected for a seven-year term by direct elections, and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Azerbaijan" title="Prime Minister of Azerbaijan">Prime Minister</a>. The president is authorized to form the Cabinet, a collective executive body, accountable to both the President and the National Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-LaPorte2016_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LaPorte2016-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The Cabinet of Azerbaijan consists primarily of the prime minister, his deputies, and ministers. The president does not have the right to dissolve the National Assembly, but has the right to veto its decisions. To override the presidential veto, the parliament must have a majority of 95 votes. The judicial power is vested in the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Azerbaijan" title="Constitutional Court of Azerbaijan">Constitutional Court</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Azerbaijan" title="Supreme Court of Azerbaijan">Supreme Court</a>, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Economic_Court_of_Azerbaijan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Economic Court of Azerbaijan (page does not exist)">Economic Court</a>. The president nominates the judges in these courts. The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission_for_the_Efficiency_of_Justice" title="European Commission for the Efficiency of Justice">European Commission for the Efficiency of Justice</a> (CEPEJ) report refers to the Azerbaijani justice model on the selection of new judges as best practice, reflecting the particular features and the course of development towards ensuring the independence and quality of the judiciary in a new democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Azerbaijan's system of governance nominally can be called two-tiered. The top or highest tier of the government is the Executive Power headed by President. The President appoints the Cabinet of Ministers and other high-ranking officials. The Local Executive Authority is merely continuation of Executive Power. The legal status of local state administration in Azerbaijan is determined by the Provision on Local Executive Authority (<i>Yerli Icra Hakimiyati</i>), adopted 16 June 1999. In June 2012, the President approved the new Regulation, which granted additional powers to Local Executive Authorities, strengthening their dominant position in Azerbaijan's local affairs<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Chapter 9 of the Constitution of the Azerbaijan Republic addresses major issues of local self-government, such as the legal status of municipalities, types of local self-government bodies, their basic powers and relationships to other official entities. The other nominal tier of governance is municipalities (<i>Bələdiyə</i>) and members of municipalities are elected by general vote in Municipal elections every five years. Currently there are 1,607 municipalities across the country. The Law on Municipal Elections and the Law on the Status of Municipalities were the first to be adopted in the field of local government (2 July 1999). The Law on Municipal Service regulates the activities of municipal employees, their rights, duties, labor conditions and social benefits, and outlines the structure of the executive apparatus and the organization of municipal service. The Law on the Status of Municipalities regulates the role and structure of municipal bodies and outlines state guarantees of legal and financial autonomy. The law pays special attention to the adoption and execution of municipal programs concerning social protection, social and economic development and the local environment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The Security Council is the deliberative body under the president, and he organizes it according to the Constitution. It was established on 10 April 1997. The administrative department is not a part of the president's office but manages the financial, technical and pecuniary activities of both the president and his office.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilham_Aliyev_and_Donald_Trump.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Ilham_Aliyev_and_Donald_Trump.jpg/220px-Ilham_Aliyev_and_Donald_Trump.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Ilham_Aliyev_and_Donald_Trump.jpg/330px-Ilham_Aliyev_and_Donald_Trump.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Ilham_Aliyev_and_Donald_Trump.jpg/440px-Ilham_Aliyev_and_Donald_Trump.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="541" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilham_Aliyev_and_Donald_Trump.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President Aliyev meeting President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> during the reception hosted by the U.S. President in New York.</div></div></div>
<p>Although Azerbaijan has held several elections since regaining its independence and it has many of the formal institutions of democracy, it remains classified as "not free" (on border with "partly free") by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-frh_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frh-128">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In recent years, large numbers of Azerbaijani journalists, bloggers, lawyers, and human rights activists have been rounded up and jailed for their criticism of President Aliyev and government authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> A resolution adopted by the European Parliament in September 2015 described Azerbaijan as "having suffered the greatest decline in democratic governance in all of Eurasia over the past ten years," noting as well that its dialogue with the country on human rights has "not made any substantial progress."<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> On 17 March 2016, the President of Azerbaijan signed a decree pardoning more than a dozen of the persons regarded as political prisoners by some NGOs.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> This decree was welcomed as a positive step by the US State Department.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> On 16 March 2017 another pardon decree was signed, which led to the release of additional persons regarded as political prisoners.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Azerbaijan has been harshly criticized for bribing foreign officials and diplomats in order to promote its causes abroad and legitimize its elections at home, a practice which has been termed as <a href="/wiki/Caviar_diplomacy" title="Caviar diplomacy">Caviar diplomacy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> However, on 6 March 2017, <a href="/wiki/European_strategic_intelligence_and_security_center" class="mw-redirect" title="European strategic intelligence and security center">ESISC</a> (European Strategic Intelligence and Security Center) published a report called "The Armenian Connection", in which it attacked human rights NGOs and research organisations criticising human rights violations and corruption in Azerbaijan.
<a href="/wiki/European_strategic_intelligence_and_security_center" class="mw-redirect" title="European strategic intelligence and security center">ESISC</a> in that report asserted that the "Caviar diplomacy" report elaborated by ESI aimed to create a climate of suspicion based on slander to form a network of MPs that would engage in a political war against Azerbaijan,and that the network, composed of European PMs, Armenian officials, and some NGOs (Human Rights Watch, Amnesty International, "Human Rights House Foundation", "Open Dialog, European Stability Initiative, and Helsinki Committee for Human Rights) was financed by the Soros Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> According to Robert Coalson (Radio Free Europe), ESISC is a part of Baku's lobbying efforts to extend the use of front think tanks to shift public opinion.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Freedom Files Analytical Centre said that "The report is written in the worst traditions of authoritarian propaganda".<sup id="cite_ref-FFAC_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFAC-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Azerbaijan" title="Foreign relations of Azerbaijan">Foreign relations of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_and_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijan and the European Union">Azerbaijan and the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan_meet_with_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan_meet_with_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg/220px-Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan_meet_with_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan_meet_with_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg/330px-Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan_meet_with_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan_meet_with_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg/440px-Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan_meet_with_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1960" data-file-height="1275" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan_meet_with_Ilham_Aliyev.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0lham_Aliyev" class="mw-redirect" title="İlham Aliyev">İlham Aliyev</a> with President of Turkey <a href="/wiki/Recep_Tayyip_Erdo%C4%9Fan" title="Recep Tayyip Erdoğan">Recep Tayyip Erdoğan</a>, 31 October 2017</div></div></div>
<p>The short-lived Azerbaijan Democratic Republic succeeded in establishing diplomatic relations with six countries, sending diplomatic representatives to Germany and Finland.<sup id="cite_ref-CSUS_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSUS-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> The process of international recognition of Azerbaijan's independence from the collapsing Soviet Union lasted roughly one year. The most recent country to recognize Azerbaijan was Bahrain, on 6 November 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Full diplomatic relations, including mutual exchanges of missions, were first established with Turkey, Pakistan, the United States, Iran<sup id="cite_ref-CSUS_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CSUS-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> and Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-israelmfa_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-israelmfa-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijan has placed a particular emphasis on its "<a href="/wiki/Special_relationship_(international_relations)" title="Special relationship (international relations)">special relationship</a>" with Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Azerbaijan has diplomatic relations with 158 countries so far and holds membership in 38 international organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-FCO_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCO-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> It holds observer status in the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> and is a correspondent at the <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">International Telecommunication Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FCO_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FCO-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> On 9 May 2006 Azerbaijan was elected to membership in the newly established <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Human Rights Council">Human Rights Council</a> by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>. The term of office began on 19 June 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijan for the first time elected as a non-permanent member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_election,_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Security Council election, 2011">UN Security Council in 2011</a> with the support of 155 countries.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Heads_of_state_attended_ceremony_to_release_young_sturgeons_into_Caspian_Sea_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Heads_of_state_attended_ceremony_to_release_young_sturgeons_into_Caspian_Sea_2.jpg/220px-Heads_of_state_attended_ceremony_to_release_young_sturgeons_into_Caspian_Sea_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Heads_of_state_attended_ceremony_to_release_young_sturgeons_into_Caspian_Sea_2.jpg/330px-Heads_of_state_attended_ceremony_to_release_young_sturgeons_into_Caspian_Sea_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Heads_of_state_attended_ceremony_to_release_young_sturgeons_into_Caspian_Sea_2.jpg/440px-Heads_of_state_attended_ceremony_to_release_young_sturgeons_into_Caspian_Sea_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1340" data-file-height="894" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Heads_of_state_attended_ceremony_to_release_young_sturgeons_into_Caspian_Sea_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">Ilham Aliyev</a> with Russian president <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> at the Caspian Sea Summit in <a href="/wiki/Aktau" title="Aktau">Aktau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, August 2018</div></div></div>
<p>Foreign policy priorities of Azerbaijan include, first of all, the restoration of its territorial integrity; elimination of the consequences of occupation of Nagorno-Karabakh and seven other regions of Azerbaijan surrounding Nagorno-Karabakh;<sup id="cite_ref-NSC_AZ_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSC_AZ-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> integration into European and Euro-Atlantic structure; contribution to international security; cooperation with international organizations; regional cooperation and bilateral relations; strengthening of defense capability; promotion of security by domestic policy means; strengthening of democracy; preservation of ethnic and religious tolerance; scientific, educational, and cultural policy and preservation of moral values; economic and social development; enhancing internal and border security; and migration, energy, and transportation security policy.<sup id="cite_ref-NSC_AZ_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSC_AZ-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Azerbaijani government, in late 2007, stated that the long-standing dispute over the Armenian-occupied territory of Nagorno-Karabakh is almost certain to spark a new war if it remains unresolved.<sup id="cite_ref-NSC_AZ_148-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSC_AZ-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The Government is in the process of increasing its military budget.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Azerbaijan is an active member of international coalitions fighting international terrorism. Azerbaijan was one of the first countries to offer support after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The country is contributing to peacekeeping efforts in Kosovo, Afghanistan and Iraq. Azerbaijan is an active member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> program. It also maintains good relations with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and could potentially one day apply for membership.<sup id="cite_ref-NSC_AZ_148-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSC_AZ-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Azerbaijan" title="Administrative divisions of Azerbaijan">Administrative divisions of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<p>Azerbaijan is divided into 10 economic regions; 66 <a href="/wiki/Raion" title="Raion">rayons</a> (<i>rayonlar</i>, singular <i>rayon</i>) and 77 cities (<i>şəhərlər</i>, singular <i>şəhər</i>) of which 12 are under the direct authority of the republic.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Moreover, Azerbaijan includes the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous Republic">Autonomous Republic</a> (<i>muxtar respublika</i>) of <a href="/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic" title="Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic">Nakhchivan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Azerbaijan" title="President of Azerbaijan">President of Azerbaijan</a> appoints the governors of these units, while the government of Nakhchivan is elected and approved by the parliament of Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_Armed_Forces" title="Azerbaijani Armed Forces">Azerbaijani Armed Forces</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azeri_navy_in_port.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/40/Azeri_navy_in_port.jpg/220px-Azeri_navy_in_port.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/40/Azeri_navy_in_port.jpg/330px-Azeri_navy_in_port.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/40/Azeri_navy_in_port.jpg/440px-Azeri_navy_in_port.jpg 2x" data-file-width="925" data-file-height="553" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azeri_navy_in_port.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_Navy" title="Azerbaijani Navy">Azerbaijani Navy</a> fleet during the 2011 military parade in Baku</div></div></div>
<p>The history of the modern Azerbaijan army dates back to <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a> in 1918, when the National Army of the newly formed Azerbaijan Democratic Republic was created on 26 June 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> When Azerbaijan gained independence after the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, the Armed Forces of the Republic of Azerbaijan were created according to the Law on the Armed Forces of 9 October 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The original date of the establishment of the short-lived National Army is celebrated as Army Day (26 June) in today's Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
As of 2002, Azerbaijan had 95,000 active personnel in its armed forces. There are also 17,000 paramilitary troops.<sup id="cite_ref-Blandy12_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blandy12-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The armed forces have three branches: the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Army of Azerbaijan">Land Forces</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_Air_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani Air Forces">Air Forces</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijan Navy">Navy</a>. Additionally the armed forces embrace several military sub-groups that can be involved in state defense when needed. These are the <a href="/wiki/Internal_Troops_(Azerbaijan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Internal Troops (Azerbaijan)">Internal Troops</a> of the Ministry of Internal Affairs and the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Border_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijan Border Guard">State Border Service</a>, which includes the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Coast_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijan Coast Guard">Coast Guard</a> as well.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_96-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_National_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijan National Guard">Azerbaijan National Guard</a> is a further paramilitary force. It operates as a semi-independent entity of the Special State Protection Service, an agency subordinate to the President.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_33.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_33.jpg/220px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_33.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_33.jpg/330px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_33.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_33.jpg/440px-%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_33.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9F%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4_%D0%B2_%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C_70-%D0%BB%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%9F%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%B4%D1%8B_-_33.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Contingent from the Azerbaijani military during the <a href="/wiki/2015_Moscow_Victory_Day_Parade" title="2015 Moscow Victory Day Parade">Moscow Victory Day Parade</a>, 9 May 2015</div></div></div>
<p>Azerbaijan adheres to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe" title="Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe">Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe</a> and has signed all major international arms and weapons treaties. Azerbaijan closely cooperates with <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> in programs such as <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">Partnership for Peace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Individual_Partnership_Action_Plan" title="Individual Partnership Action Plan">Individual Partnership Action Plan</a>. Azerbaijan has deployed 151 of its Peacekeeping Forces in Iraq and another 184 in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The defense budget of Azerbaijan for 2011 was set at US$3.1&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-ng.ru_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ng.ru-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> In addition to that, $1.36&#160;billion was planned to be used for the needs of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_Industry_of_Azerbaijan" title="Ministry of Defence Industry of Azerbaijan">defense industry</a>, which bring up the total military budget to 4.6 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-ng.ru_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ng.ru-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijani President Ilham Aliyev said on 26 June 2011 that the defence spending reached $3.3&#160;billion that year.<sup id="cite_ref-AFP_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Azerbaijan's defense budget for 2013 is $3.7&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Economist_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Economist-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Azerbaijani defense industry manufactures small arms, artillery systems, tanks, armors and <a href="/wiki/Night_vision_device" class="mw-redirect" title="Night vision device">noctovision devices</a>, aviation bombs, pilotless vehicles, various military vehicles and military planes and helicopters.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Azerbaijan" title="Economy of Azerbaijan">Economy of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<p>After gaining independence in 1991, Azerbaijan became a member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Bank_for_Reconstruction_and_Development" title="European Bank for Reconstruction and Development">European Bank for Reconstruction and Development</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Development_Bank" title="Islamic Development Bank">Islamic Development Bank</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AZE_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AZE-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The banking system of Azerbaijan consists of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Azerbaijan" title="Central Bank of Azerbaijan">Central Bank of Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commercial_bank" title="Commercial bank">commercial banks</a> and non-banking credit organizations. The National (now Central) Bank was created in 1992 based on the Azerbaijan State Savings Bank, an affiliate of the former State Savings Bank of the USSR. The Central Bank serves as Azerbaijan's central bank, empowered to issue the national currency, the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_manat" title="Azerbaijani manat">Azerbaijani manat</a>, and to supervise all commercial banks. Two major commercial banks are <a href="/w/index.php?title=UniBank_(Azerbaijan)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="UniBank (Azerbaijan) (page does not exist)">UniBank</a> and the state-owned <a href="/wiki/International_Bank_of_Azerbaijan" title="International Bank of Azerbaijan">International Bank of Azerbaijan</a>, run by <a href="/wiki/Jahangir_Hajiyev" title="Jahangir Hajiyev">Dr. Jahangir Hajiyev</a>.
</p><p>Pushed up by spending and demand growth, the 2007 <a href="/wiki/First_quarter_of_a_calendar_year" class="mw-redirect" title="First quarter of a calendar year">Q1</a> inflation rate reached 16.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-INF_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INF-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Nominal incomes and monthly wages climbed 29% and 25% respectively against this figure, but price increases in non-oil industry encouraged inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-INF_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INF-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijan shows some signs of the so-called "<a href="/wiki/Dutch_disease" title="Dutch disease">Dutch disease</a>" because of its fast-growing energy sector, which causes inflation and makes non-energy exports more expensive.
</p><p>In the early 2000s the chronically high inflation was brought under control. This led to the launch of a new currency, the new Azerbaijani manat, on 1 January 2006, to cement the economic reforms and erase the vestiges of an unstable economy.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, Azerbaijan was cited as one of the top 10 reformers by the World Bank's <a href="/wiki/Doing_Business_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="Doing Business Report">Doing Business Report</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Azerbaijan led the world as the top reformer in 2007/08, with improvements on seven out of 10 indicators of regulatory reform. Azerbaijan started operating a one-stop shop in January 2008 that halved the time, cost and number of procedures to start a business. Business registrations increased by 40% in the first six months. Azerbaijan also eliminated the minimum loan cutoff of $1,100, more than doubling the number of borrowers covered by the credit registry. Also, taxpayers can now file forms and pay their taxes online. Azerbaijan's extensive reforms moved it far up the ranks, from 97 to 33 in the overall ease of doing business.
</p></blockquote>
<p>Azerbaijan is also ranked 57th in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a> for 2010–2011, above other CIS countries.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> By 2012 the <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> of Azerbaijan had increased 20-fold from to its 1995 level.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Doing_Business_report" class="mw-redirect" title="Doing Business report">Doing Business report</a> 2019, Azerbaijan improved its position in the Ease of doing business rank from 57 to 25.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> As a result of implementing a record number of reforms mainly involving institutional changes among the 10 top improvers, to do business in Azerbaijan became easier, such as time and cost to get construction permit reduced significantly (time by 80 days and cost by 12.563 <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_manat" title="Azerbaijani manat">AZN</a>), process of connecting electricity grid rationalized, as well as getting credit simplified.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Azerbaijan" title="Energy in Azerbaijan">Energy in Azerbaijan</a></div> <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Petroleum_industry_in_Azerbaijan" title="Petroleum industry in Azerbaijan">Petroleum industry in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_pump_in_Baku.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_pump_in_Baku.jpg/220px-Oil_pump_in_Baku.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_pump_in_Baku.jpg/330px-Oil_pump_in_Baku.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Oil_pump_in_Baku.jpg/440px-Oil_pump_in_Baku.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2237" data-file-height="1520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Oil_pump_in_Baku.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Pumpjack" title="Pumpjack">pumping unit</a> for the mechanical extraction of oil on the outskirts of Baku</div></div></div>
<p>Two-thirds of Azerbaijan is rich in oil and natural gas.<sup id="cite_ref-AZ_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AZ-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baku_pipelines.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Baku_pipelines.svg/220px-Baku_pipelines.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Baku_pipelines.svg/330px-Baku_pipelines.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Baku_pipelines.svg/440px-Baku_pipelines.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1316" data-file-height="762" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baku_pipelines.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus_Pipeline" title="South Caucasus Pipeline">South Caucasus Pipeline</a> is bringing natural gas through Turkey to Europe</div></div></div>
<p>The history of the oil industry of Azerbaijan dates back to the ancient period. Arabian historian and traveler Ahmed Al-Belaruri discussed the economy of the Absheron peninsula in anntiquity, mentioning its oil in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> There are lots of <a href="/wiki/Pipelines_in_Azerbaijan" title="Pipelines in Azerbaijan">pipelines in Azerbaijan</a>.
</p><p>The region of the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Caucasus" title="Lesser Caucasus">Lesser Caucasus</a> accounts for most of the country's gold, silver, iron, copper, <a href="/wiki/Titanium" title="Titanium">titanium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chromium" title="Chromium">chromium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manganese" title="Manganese">manganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobalt" title="Cobalt">cobalt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molybdenum" title="Molybdenum">molybdenum</a>, complex <a href="/wiki/Ore" title="Ore">ore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antimony" title="Antimony">antimony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AZ_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AZ-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> In September 1994, a 30-year contract was signed between the <a href="/wiki/State_Oil_Company_of_Azerbaijan_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="State Oil Company of Azerbaijan Republic">State Oil Company of Azerbaijan Republic</a> (SOCAR) and 13&#160;oil companies, among them <a href="/wiki/Amoco" title="Amoco">Amoco</a>, <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a>, <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lukoil" title="Lukoil">Lukoil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equinor" title="Equinor">Equinor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AZE_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AZE-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> As Western oil companies are able to tap deepwater <a href="/wiki/Oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil field">oilfields</a> untouched by the Soviet exploitation, Azerbaijan is considered one of the most important spots in the world for <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">oil exploration</a> and development.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, the <a href="/wiki/State_Oil_Fund_of_Azerbaijan" title="State Oil Fund of Azerbaijan">State Oil Fund of Azerbaijan</a> was established as an extra-budgetary fund to ensure <a href="/wiki/Macroeconomy" class="mw-redirect" title="Macroeconomy">macroeconomic</a> stability, transparency in the management of oil revenue, and safeguarding of resources for future generations.
</p><p>Azeriqaz, a sub-company of SOCAR, intends to ensure full gasification of the country by 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
Azerbaijan is one of the sponsors of the East–West and North–South energy transport corridors. Baku–Tbilisi–Kars railway line will connect the Caspian region with Turkey, is expected to be completed in July 2017. The Trans-Anatolian Natural Gas Pipeline (TANAP) and Trans-Adriatic Pipeline (TAP) will deliver natural gas from Azerbaijan's Shah Deniz gas to Turkey and Europe.
</p><p>Azerbaijan extended the agreement on development of <a href="/wiki/Azeri%E2%80%93Chirag%E2%80%93Gunashli" title="Azeri–Chirag–Gunashli">ACG</a> until 2050 according to the amended <a href="/wiki/Production_sharing_agreement" title="Production sharing agreement">PSA</a> signed on 14 September 2017 by <a href="/wiki/SOCAR" title="SOCAR">SOCAR</a> and co-venturers (<a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Corporation" title="Chevron Corporation">Chevron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inpex" title="Inpex">INPEX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equinor" title="Equinor">Equinor</a>, <a href="/wiki/ExxonMobil" title="ExxonMobil">ExxonMobil</a>, <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkiye_Petrolleri_Anonim_Ortakl%C4%B1%C4%9F%C4%B1" title="Türkiye Petrolleri Anonim Ortaklığı">TP</a>, ITOCHU and <a href="/wiki/Oil_and_Natural_Gas_Corporation" title="Oil and Natural Gas Corporation">ONGC Videsh</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Azerbaijan" title="Agriculture in Azerbaijan">Agriculture in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<p>Azerbaijan has the largest agricultural basin in the region. About 54.9 percent of Azerbaijan is agricultural land.<sup id="cite_ref-STA_112-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-STA-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> At the beginning of 2007 there were 4,755,100&#160;hectares of utilized agricultural area.<sup id="cite_ref-AG_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AG-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> In the same year the total wood resources counted 136 million m³.<sup id="cite_ref-AG_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AG-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijan's agricultural scientific research institutes are focused on meadows and pastures, horticulture and <a href="/wiki/Subtropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical">subtropical</a> crops, green vegetables, <a href="/wiki/Viticulture" title="Viticulture">viticulture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_wine" title="Azerbaijani wine">wine-making</a>, cotton growing and <a href="/wiki/Medicinal_plants" title="Medicinal plants">medicinal plants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> In some areas it is profitable to grow grain, potatoes, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_beet" title="Sugar beet">sugar beets</a>, cotton<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> and tobacco. Livestock, dairy products, and wine and <a href="/wiki/Distilled_spirit" class="mw-redirect" title="Distilled spirit">spirits</a> are also important farm products. The Caspian <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry" title="Fishing industry">fishing industry</a> concentrates on the dwindling stocks of <a href="/wiki/Sturgeon" title="Sturgeon">sturgeon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beluga_(sturgeon)" title="Beluga (sturgeon)">beluga</a>. In 2002 the Azerbaijani <a href="/wiki/Merchant_marine" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchant marine">merchant marine</a> had 54 ships.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some products previously imported from abroad have begun to be produced locally. Among them are Coca-Cola by Coca-Cola Bottlers LTD., beer by Baki-Kastel, parquet by Nehir and oil pipes by EUPEC Pipe Coating Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Azerbaijan" title="Tourism in Azerbaijan">Tourism in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shahdag01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Shahdag01.jpg/220px-Shahdag01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Shahdag01.jpg/330px-Shahdag01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Shahdag01.jpg/440px-Shahdag01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7360" data-file-height="4912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shahdag01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Shahdag_Mountain_Resort" title="Shahdag Mountain Resort">Shahdag Mountain Resort</a> is the country's largest winter resort.</div></div></div>
<p>Tourism is an important part of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Azerbaijan" title="Economy of Azerbaijan">economy of Azerbaijan</a>. The country was a well-known tourist spot in the 1980s. However, the fall of the Soviet Union, and the <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="Nagorno-Karabakh War">Nagorno-Karabakh War</a> during the 1990s, damaged the tourist industry and the image of Azerbaijan as a tourist destination.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was not until the 2000s that the tourism industry began to recover, and the country has since experienced a high rate of growth in the number of tourist visits and overnight stays.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> In the recent years, Azerbaijan has also become a popular destination for religious, spa, and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_medical_tourism" title="Azerbaijani medical tourism">health care tourism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Baku_Boom_Has_Yet_to_Hit_Regions_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baku_Boom_Has_Yet_to_Hit_Regions-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> During winter, the <a href="/wiki/Shahdag_Mountain_Resort" title="Shahdag Mountain Resort">Shahdag Mountain Resort</a> offers skiing with state of the art facilities.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Azerbaijan">government of Azerbaijan</a> has set the development of Azerbaijan as an elite tourist destination as a top priority. It is a national strategy to make tourism a major, if not the single largest, contributor to the Azerbaijani economy.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> These activities are regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Culture_and_Tourism_(Azerbaijan)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Culture and Tourism (Azerbaijan)">Ministry of Culture and Tourism of Azerbaijan</a>.
There are 63 countries which have visa-free score.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
E-visa<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> – for a visit of foreigners of visa-required countries to the Republic of Azerbaijan.
</p><p>According to Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report 2015 of the World Economic Forum, Azerbaijan holds 84th place.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a report by the World Travel and Tourism Council, Azerbaijan was among the top ten countries showing the strongest growth in visitor exports between 2010 and 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> In addition, Azerbaijan placed first (46.1%) among countries with the fastest-developing travel and tourism economies, with strong indicators for inbound international visitor spending last year.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Transportation in Azerbaijan">Transportation in Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Azerbaijan" title="Rail transport in Azerbaijan">Rail transport in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<p>The convenient location of Azerbaijan on the crossroad of major international traffic arteries, such as the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> and the south–north corridor, highlights the strategic importance of transportation sector for the country's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The transport sector in the country includes roads, railways, aviation, and maritime transport.
</p><p>Azerbaijan is also an important economic hub in the transportation of raw materials. The <a href="/wiki/Baku%E2%80%93Tbilisi%E2%80%93Ceyhan_pipeline" title="Baku–Tbilisi–Ceyhan pipeline">Baku–Tbilisi–Ceyhan pipeline</a> (BTC) became operational in May 2006 and extends more than 1,774&#160;kilometers through the territories of Azerbaijan, Georgia and Turkey. The BTC is designed to transport up to 50&#160;million tons of crude oil annually and carries oil from the Caspian Sea oilfields to global markets.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/South_Caucasus_Pipeline" title="South Caucasus Pipeline">South Caucasus Pipeline</a>, also stretching through the territory of Azerbaijan, Georgia, and Turkey, became operational at the end of 2006 and offers additional gas supplies to the European market from the <a href="/wiki/Shah_Deniz_gas_field" title="Shah Deniz gas field">Shah Deniz gas field</a>. Shah Deniz is expected to produce up to 296&#160;billion cubic meters of natural gas per year.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijan also plays a major role in the EU-sponsored Silk Road Project.
</p><p>In 2002, the Azerbaijani government established the Ministry of Transport with a broad range of policy and regulatory functions. In the same year, the country became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Convention_on_Road_Traffic" title="Vienna Convention on Road Traffic">Vienna Convention on Road Traffic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> Priorities are upgrading the transport network and improving transportation services in order to better facilitate the development of other sectors of the economy.
</p><p>The 2012 construction of <a href="/wiki/Kars%E2%80%93Tbilisi%E2%80%93Baku_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Kars–Tbilisi–Baku railway">Kars–Tbilisi–Baku railway</a> was meant to improve transportation between Asia and Europe by connecting the railways of China and Kazakhstan in the east to the European railway system in the west via Turkey. In 2010 <a href="/wiki/Russian_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian gauge">Broad-gauge</a> railways and electrified railways stretched for 2,918&#160;km (1,813&#160;mi) and 1,278&#160;km (794&#160;mi) respectively. By 2010, there were 35 airports and one <a href="/wiki/Heliport" title="Heliport">heliport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_96-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Communications in Azerbaijan">Communications in Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_National_Aerospace_Agency" title="Azerbaijan National Aerospace Agency">Azerbaijan National Aerospace Agency</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Azerbaijani_inventions_and_discoveries" title="List of Azerbaijani inventions and discoveries">List of Azerbaijani inventions and discoveries</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shamakhi_observatory.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Shamakhi_observatory.jpg/220px-Shamakhi_observatory.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Shamakhi_observatory.jpg/330px-Shamakhi_observatory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Shamakhi_observatory.jpg/440px-Shamakhi_observatory.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="332" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shamakhi_observatory.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Shamakhi_Astrophysical_Observatory" title="Shamakhi Astrophysical Observatory">Shamakhi Astrophysical Observatory</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the 21st century, a new oil and gas boom helped to improve the situation in Azerbaijan's science and technology sectors, and the government launched a campaign aimed at modernization and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Azerbaijani_inventions_and_discoveries" title="List of Azerbaijani inventions and discoveries">innovation</a>. The government estimates that profits from the information technology and communication industry will grow and become comparable to those from oil production.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Azerbaijan has a large and steadily growing Internet sector, mostly uninfluenced by the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%932012_global_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2007–2012 global financial crisis">global financial crisis</a>; rapid growth is forecast for at least five more years.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The country has also been making progress in developing its telecoms sector. The Ministry of Communications &amp; Information Technologies (MCIT), as well as being an operator through its role in Aztelekom, is both a policy-maker and regulator. Public pay phones are available for local calls and require the purchase of a token from the telephone exchange or some shops and kiosks. Tokens allow a call of indefinite duration. As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Azerbaijan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there were 1,397,000 main telephone lines<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> and 1,485,000 internet users.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> There are four <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a> providers: <a href="/wiki/Azercell" title="Azercell">Azercell</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bakcell&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bakcell (page does not exist)">Bakcell</a>, Azerfon (<a href="/wiki/Nar_Mobile" title="Nar Mobile">Nar Mobile</a>), <a href="/wiki/Nakhtel" title="Nakhtel">Nakhtel</a> mobile network operators and one <a href="/wiki/CDMA" class="mw-redirect" title="CDMA">CDMA</a>.
</p><p>In the 21st century a number of prominent Azerbaijani <a href="/wiki/Geodynamics" title="Geodynamics">geodynamics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geotectonics" class="mw-redirect" title="Geotectonics">geotectonics</a> scientists, inspired by the fundamental works of Elchin Khalilov and others, designed hundreds of earthquake prediction stations and earthquake-resistant buildings that now constitute the bulk of The Republican Center of Seismic Service.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_National_Aerospace_Agency" title="Azerbaijan National Aerospace Agency">Azerbaijan National Aerospace Agency</a> launched its first satellite <a href="/wiki/AzerSat_1" class="mw-redirect" title="AzerSat 1">AzerSat 1</a> into orbit on 7 February 2013 from <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Guiana Space Centre">Guiana Space Centre</a> in French Guiana at orbital positions 46° East.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> The satellite covers Europe and a significant part of Asia and Africa and serves the transmission of TV and radio broadcasting as well as the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The launching of a satellite into orbit is Azerbaijan's first step in realizing its goal of becoming a nation with its own space industry, capable of successfully implementing more projects in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Azerbaijan" title="Demographics of Azerbaijan">Demographics of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minorities_in_Azerbaijan" title="Ethnic minorities in Azerbaijan">Ethnic minorities in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Aserbaidschan_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Aserbaidschan_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Aserbaidschan_2016.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Aserbaidschan_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Aserbaidschan_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Aserbaidschan_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Aserbaidschan_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Aserbaidschan_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid</div></div></div>
<p>as of January&#160;2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Azerbaijan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 52.8% of Azerbaijan's total population of 9,981,457 is <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban</a>, with the remaining 47.2% being rural. 50.1% of the total population is female. The <a href="/wiki/Human_sex_ratio" title="Human sex ratio">sex ratio</a> in the same year was 0.99 males per female.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2011 population growth-rate was 0.85%, compared to 1.09% worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_96-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> A significant factor restricting population growth is a high level of migration. In 2011 Azerbaijan saw a migration of −1.14/1,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_96-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_diaspora" title="Azerbaijani diaspora">Azerbaijani diaspora</a> is found in 42 countries<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> and in turn there are many centers for ethnic minorities inside Azerbaijan, including the <a href="/wiki/Germans_in_Azerbaijan" title="Germans in Azerbaijan">German</a> cultural society "Karelhaus", <a href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic peoples">Slavic</a> cultural center, Azerbaijani-Israeli community, <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish people">Kurdish</a> cultural center, International <a href="/wiki/Talysh_people" title="Talysh people">Talysh</a> Association, <a href="/wiki/Lezgins" title="Lezgins">Lezgin</a> national center "Samur", Azerbaijani-<a href="/wiki/Tatarstan" title="Tatarstan">Tatar</a> community, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Crimean Tatars</a> society, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-MIN_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIN-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>

<p>The ethnic composition of the population according to the 2009 population census: 91.60% <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani people">Azerbaijanis</a>, 2.02% <a href="/wiki/Lezgians" class="mw-redirect" title="Lezgians">Lezgians</a>, 1.35% <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a> (almost all Armenians live in the break-away region of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Nagorno-Karabakh" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>), 1.34% <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, 1.26% <a href="/wiki/Talysh_people" title="Talysh people">Talysh</a>, 0.56% <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_Avars" class="mw-redirect" title="Caucasian Avars">Avars</a>, 0.43% <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a>, 0.29% <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a>, 0.28% <a href="/wiki/Tat_people_(Caucasus)" title="Tat people (Caucasus)">Tats</a>, 0.24% <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a>, 0.14% <a href="/wiki/Tsakhur_people" title="Tsakhur people">Tsakhurs</a>, 0.11% <a href="/wiki/Georgians" title="Georgians">Georgians</a>, 0.10% <a href="/wiki/Jew" class="mw-redirect" title="Jew">Jews</a>, 0.07% <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish people">Kurds</a>, other 0.21%.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanization">Urbanization</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Azerbaijan" title="List of cities in Azerbaijan">List of cities in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<p>In total, Azerbaijan has 78 cities, 63 city districts, and one special legal status city. These are followed by 261 urban-type settlements and 4248 villages.<sup id="cite_ref-stat.gov.az_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat.gov.az-219">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Azerbaijan" title="Languages of Azerbaijan">Languages of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<p>The official language is <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/Turkic_languages" title="Turkic languages">Turkic language</a>. Azerbaijani is spoken by approximately 92% of the population as a <a href="/wiki/Mother_tongue" class="mw-redirect" title="Mother tongue">mother tongue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNLANGDATA_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNLANGDATA-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> Russian and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a> (only in Nagorno-Karabakh) are also spoken, and each are the mother tongue of around 1.5% of the population respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-UNLANGDATA_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNLANGDATA-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> Russian and English play significant roles as second or third languages of education and communication.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> There are a dozen other minority languages spoken natively in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Avar_language" title="Avar language">Avar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budukh_language" title="Budukh language">Budukh</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juhuri_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Juhuri language">Juhuri</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages_222-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Khinalug_language" title="Khinalug language">Khinalug</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages_222-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kryts_language" title="Kryts language">Kryts</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages_222-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lezgian_language" title="Lezgian language">Lezgian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rutul_language" title="Rutul language">Rutul</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages_222-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Talysh_language" title="Talysh language">Talysh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tat_language_(Caucasus)" title="Tat language (Caucasus)">Tat</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages_222-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tsakhur_language" title="Tsakhur language">Tsakhur</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages_222-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Udi_language" title="Udi language">Udi</a><sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages_222-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_the_World&#39;s_Endangered_Languages-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> are all spoken by small minorities. Some of these language communities are very small and their numbers are decreasing.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Armenian is almost exclusively spoken in the break-away Nagorno-Karabakh region.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
<tbody><tr style="background:#ddd"><th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religions in Azerbaijan<sup id="cite_ref-BCRPWA_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BCRPWA-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup></th></tr>
<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">
<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;"></td>
<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>
<td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td>
<td style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;"></td>
<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Islam</td>
<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:green; width:97.4%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>
<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">97.4%</td>
