</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Azerbaijan" title="Religion in Azerbaijan">Religion in Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Azerbaijan" title="Freedom of religion in Azerbaijan">Freedom of religion in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bibi_Heybat_Mosque_Baku_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Bibi_Heybat_Mosque_Baku_1.jpg/220px-Bibi_Heybat_Mosque_Baku_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Bibi_Heybat_Mosque_Baku_1.jpg/330px-Bibi_Heybat_Mosque_Baku_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Bibi_Heybat_Mosque_Baku_1.jpg/440px-Bibi_Heybat_Mosque_Baku_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="894" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bibi_Heybat_Mosque_Baku_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Bibi-Heybat_Mosque" title="Bibi-Heybat Mosque">Bibi-Heybat Mosque</a> in Baku. The mosque is built over the tomb of a descendant of <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bibi_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bibi-225">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Around 97% of the population are Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> 85% of the Muslims are <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Muslims</a> and 15% <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslims</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> and the Republic of Azerbaijan has the second highest Shia population percentage in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Other faiths are practised by the country's various ethnic groups. Under article 48 of its <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Azerbaijan" title="Constitution of Azerbaijan">Constitution</a>, Azerbaijan is a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a> and ensures religious freedom. In a 2006–2008 <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup</a> poll, only 21% of respondents from Azerbaijan stated that religion is an important part of their daily lives. This makes Azerbaijan the least religious Muslim-majority country in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Of the nation's religious minorities, the estimated 280,000 Christians (3.1%)<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> are mostly <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgian_Orthodox_Church" title="Georgian Orthodox Church">Georgian</a> <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic</a> (almost all Armenians live in the break-away region of Nagorno-Karabakh).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_96-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, there were 250 <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Other Christian denominations as of 2002 include <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutherans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Molokan" title="Molokan">Molokans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AZR_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AZR-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> There is also a small <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> community.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijan also has an ancient <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> population with a 2,000-year history; Jewish organizations estimate that 12,000 Jews remain in Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijan also is home to members of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith">Bahá'í</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Society_for_Krishna_Consciousness" title="International Society for Krishna Consciousness">Hare Krishna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> communities, as well as adherents of the other religious communities.<sup id="cite_ref-AZR_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AZR-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Some religious communities have been <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Azerbaijan#Restrictions_on_religious_freedom" title="Freedom of religion in Azerbaijan">unofficially restricted from religious freedom</a>. A <a href="/wiki/U.S._State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. State Department">U.S. State Department</a> report on the matter mentions detention of members of certain Muslim and Christian groups, and many groups have difficulty registering with the SCWRA.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Azerbaijan" title="Education in Azerbaijan">Education in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dunya1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Dunya1.jpg/220px-Dunya1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Dunya1.jpg/330px-Dunya1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Dunya1.jpg/440px-Dunya1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dunya1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Classroom in <a href="/wiki/Khazar_University" title="Khazar University">Dunya School</a></div></div></div>
<p>A relatively high percentage of Azerbaijanis have obtained some form of higher education, most notably in scientific and technical subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-AZ_study_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AZ_study-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> In the Soviet era, literacy and average education levels rose dramatically from their very low starting point, despite two changes in the standard alphabet, from <a href="/wiki/Perso-Arabic_script" class="mw-redirect" title="Perso-Arabic script">Perso-Arabic script</a> to <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin</a> in the 1920s and from Roman to <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyrillic">Cyrillic</a> in the 1930s. According to Soviet data, 100 percent of males and females (ages nine to forty-nine) were literate in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-AZ_study_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AZ_study-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Development Program">United Nations Development Program</a> Report 2009, the literacy rate in Azerbaijan is 99.5 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since independence, one of the first laws that Azerbaijan's Parliament passed to disassociate itself from the Soviet Union was to adopt a <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_alphabet" title="Azerbaijani alphabet">modified-Latin alphabet</a> to replace Cyrillic.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Other than that the Azerbaijani system has undergone little structural change. Initial alterations have included the reestablishment of religious education (banned during the Soviet period) and curriculum changes that have reemphasized the use of the Azerbaijani language and have eliminated ideological content. In addition to elementary schools, the education institutions include thousands of preschools, general secondary schools, and <a href="/wiki/Vocational_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Vocational schools">vocational schools</a>, including specialized secondary schools and technical schools. Education through the eighth grade is compulsory.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Azerbaijan" title="Culture of Azerbaijan">Culture of Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Literature of Azerbaijan">Literature of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Intangible_Cultural_Heritage_List_in_Azerbaijan" title="UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage List in Azerbaijan">UNESCO Intangible Cultural Heritage List in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:388px;max-width:388px"><div class="trow"><div class="theader" style="text-align:center;background-color:transparent">The <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_rug" title="Azerbaijani rug">Azerbaijani carpet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kalaghai" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalaghai">Kalaghai</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpiece of Intangible Heritage of Humanity</a>.</div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:182px;max-width:182px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbaijani_Afshan_rug.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Azerbaijani carpet &quot;Afshan&quot;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Azerbaijani_Afshan_rug.jpg/180px-Azerbaijani_Afshan_rug.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="130" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Azerbaijani_Afshan_rug.jpg/270px-Azerbaijani_Afshan_rug.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Azerbaijani_Afshan_rug.jpg/360px-Azerbaijani_Afshan_rug.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1036" data-file-height="749" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Az%C9%99rbaycan_ip%C9%99yind%C9%99n_k%C9%99la%C4%9Fay%C4%B1lar_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Silk Kalaghais" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Az%C9%99rbaycan_ip%C9%99yind%C9%99n_k%C9%99la%C4%9Fay%C4%B1lar_1.JPG/200px-Az%C9%99rbaycan_ip%C9%99yind%C9%99n_k%C9%99la%C4%9Fay%C4%B1lar_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Az%C9%99rbaycan_ip%C9%99yind%C9%99n_k%C9%99la%C4%9Fay%C4%B1lar_1.JPG/300px-Az%C9%99rbaycan_ip%C9%99yind%C9%99n_k%C9%99la%C4%9Fay%C4%B1lar_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Az%C9%99rbaycan_ip%C9%99yind%C9%99n_k%C9%99la%C4%9Fay%C4%B1lar_1.JPG/400px-Az%C9%99rbaycan_ip%C9%99yind%C9%99n_k%C9%99la%C4%9Fay%C4%B1lar_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The culture of Azerbaijan has developed as a result of many influences. Today, national traditions are well preserved in the country despite Western influences, including <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalized</a> consumer culture. Some of the main elements of the Azerbaijani culture are: music, literature, folk dances and art, cuisine, architecture, cinematography and <a href="/wiki/Novruz_in_Azerbaijan" title="Novruz in Azerbaijan">Novruz Bayram</a>. The latter is derived from the traditional celebration of the New Year in the ancient Iranian religion of <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>. Novruz is a family holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The profile of Azerbaijan's population consists, as stated above, of Azerbaijanis, as well as other nationalities or ethnic groups, compactly living in various areas of the country. Azerbaijani national and traditional dresses are the <a href="/wiki/Chokha" title="Chokha">Chokha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Papakhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Papakhi">Papakhi</a>. There are radio broadcasts in Russian, <a href="/wiki/Georgian_language" title="Georgian language">Georgian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kurdish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kurdish language">Kurdish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lezgian_language" title="Lezgian language">Lezgian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Talysh_language" title="Talysh language">Talysh</a> languages, which are financed from the state budget.<sup id="cite_ref-MIN_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIN-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Some local radio stations in <a href="/wiki/Balak%C9%99n" title="Balakən">Balakan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khachmaz_(city)" title="Khachmaz (city)">Khachmaz</a> organize broadcasts in <a href="/wiki/Avar_language" title="Avar language">Avar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tat_language_(Caucasus)" title="Tat language (Caucasus)">Tat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MIN_218-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIN-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> In Baku several newspapers are published in Russian, Kurdish (<i>Dengi Kurd</i>), Lezgian (<i>Samur</i>) and Talysh languages.<sup id="cite_ref-MIN_218-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIN-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Jewish society "Sokhnut" publishes the newspaper <i>Aziz</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-MIN_218-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIN-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_folk_dances">Music and folk dances</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Azerbaijan" title="Music of Azerbaijan">Music of Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_dances" title="Azerbaijani dances">Azerbaijani dances</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Czeyir_Hac%C4%B1b%C9%99yov6.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/%C3%9Czeyir_Hac%C4%B1b%C9%99yov6.gif/170px-%C3%9Czeyir_Hac%C4%B1b%C9%99yov6.gif" decoding="async" width="170" height="246" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3f/%C3%9Czeyir_Hac%C4%B1b%C9%99yov6.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="189" data-file-height="273" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%9Czeyir_Hac%C4%B1b%C9%99yov6.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Uzeyir_Hajibeyov" title="Uzeyir Hajibeyov">Uzeyir Hajibeyov</a> merged traditional <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani music">Azerbaijani music</a> with Western styles in the early 20th century.</div></div></div>
<p>Music of Azerbaijan builds on <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk traditions</a> that reach back nearly a thousand years.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> For centuries Azerbaijani music has evolved under the badge of <a href="/wiki/Monody" title="Monody">monody</a>, producing rhythmically diverse melodies.<sup id="cite_ref-EMD_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMD-245">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijani music has a branchy <a href="/wiki/Musical_mode" class="mw-redirect" title="Musical mode">mode</a> system, where <a href="/wiki/Chromaticism" title="Chromaticism">chromatization</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_and_minor" title="Major and minor">major and minor</a> <a href="/wiki/Musical_scale" class="mw-redirect" title="Musical scale">scales</a> is of great importance.<sup id="cite_ref-EMD_245-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EMD-245">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> Among national musical instruments there are 14 <a href="/wiki/String_instrument" title="String instrument">string instruments</a>, eight percussion instruments and six wind instruments.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Grove_Dictionary_of_Music_and_Musicians" title="The New Grove Dictionary of Music and Musicians">The Grove Dictionary of Music and Musicians</a></i>, "in terms of ethnicity, culture and religion the Azerbaijani are musically much closer to Iran than Turkey."<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbaijani_Mugam_trio_in_XVI_century_miniature_of_Nizami_Ganjavi%27s_Khosrow_and_Shirin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Azerbaijani_Mugam_trio_in_XVI_century_miniature_of_Nizami_Ganjavi%27s_Khosrow_and_Shirin.jpg/220px-Azerbaijani_Mugam_trio_in_XVI_century_miniature_of_Nizami_Ganjavi%27s_Khosrow_and_Shirin.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Azerbaijani_Mugam_trio_in_XVI_century_miniature_of_Nizami_Ganjavi%27s_Khosrow_and_Shirin.jpg/330px-Azerbaijani_Mugam_trio_in_XVI_century_miniature_of_Nizami_Ganjavi%27s_Khosrow_and_Shirin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Azerbaijani_Mugam_trio_in_XVI_century_miniature_of_Nizami_Ganjavi%27s_Khosrow_and_Shirin.jpg/440px-Azerbaijani_Mugam_trio_in_XVI_century_miniature_of_Nizami_Ganjavi%27s_Khosrow_and_Shirin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1911" data-file-height="1218" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbaijani_Mugam_trio_in_XVI_century_miniature_of_Nizami_Ganjavi%27s_Khosrow_and_Shirin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Mugham" title="Mugham">Azerbaijani Mugam</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpiece of Intangible Heritage of Humanity</a> 16th-century miniature of <a href="/wiki/Nizami_Ganjavi" title="Nizami Ganjavi">Nizami Ganjavi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Khosrow_and_Shirin" title="Khosrow and Shirin">Khosrow and Shirin</a> tragic romance</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mugham" title="Mugham">Mugham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meykhana" title="Meykhana">meykhana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Azerbaijani_ashiqs" class="mw-redirect" title="Art of Azerbaijani ashiqs">ashiq art</a> are among the many musical traditions of Azerbaijan. Mugham is usually a suite with poetry and instrumental interludes. When performing mugham, the singers have to transform their emotions into singing and music. In contrast to the mugham traditions of Central Asian countries, Azerbaijani mugham is more free-form and less rigid; it is often compared to the improvised field of <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> proclaimed the Azerbaijani mugham tradition a <a href="/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity</a> on 7 November 2003. Meykhana is a kind of traditional Azerbaijani distinctive folk unaccompanied song, usually performed by several people improvising on a particular subject.
</p><p>Ashiq combines poetry, storytelling, dance and vocal and instrumental music into a traditional performance art that stands as a symbol of Azerbaijani culture. It is a mystic troubadour or traveling bard who sings and plays the <a href="/wiki/Baglama" class="mw-redirect" title="Baglama">saz</a>. This tradition has its origin in the <a href="/wiki/Shamanistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Shamanistic">Shamanistic</a> beliefs of ancient <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic peoples</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-European_University_Institute,_Florence,_Italy_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_University_Institute,_Florence,_Italy-249">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Ashiqs' songs are semi-improvised around common bases. Azerbaijan's ashiq art was included in the list of <a href="/wiki/Intangible_Cultural_Heritage" class="mw-redirect" title="Intangible Cultural Heritage">Intangible Cultural Heritage</a> by the UNESCO on 30 September 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the mid-1960s, Western-influenced <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_pop_music" title="Azerbaijani pop music">Azerbaijani pop music</a>, in its various forms, that has been growing in popularity in Azerbaijan, while genres such as <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_rock" title="Azerbaijani rock">rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_hip_hop" title="Azerbaijani hip hop">hip hop</a> are widely produced and enjoyed. Azerbaijani pop and <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_folk_music" title="Azerbaijani folk music">Azerbaijani folk music</a> arose with the international popularity of performers like <a href="/wiki/Alim_Qasimov" title="Alim Qasimov">Alim Qasimov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rashid_Behbudov" title="Rashid Behbudov">Rashid Behbudov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vagif_Mustafazadeh" title="Vagif Mustafazadeh">Vagif Mustafazadeh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Magomayev_(musician)" title="Muslim Magomayev (musician)">Muslim Magomayev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shovkat_Alakbarova" title="Shovkat Alakbarova">Shovkat Alakbarova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rubaba_Muradova" title="Rubaba Muradova">Rubaba Muradova</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijan is an enthusiastic participant in the Eurovision Song Contest. Azerbaijan made its debut appearance at the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2008" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2008">Eurovision Song Contest</a>. The country's <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest_2009" title="Azerbaijan in the Eurovision Song Contest 2009">entry</a> gained third place in 2009 and fifth the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eldar_%26_Nigar" class="mw-redirect" title="Eldar &amp; Nigar">Ell and Nikki</a> won the first place at the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2011" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2011">Eurovision Song Contest 2011</a> with the song "<a href="/wiki/Running_Scared_(Eldar_%26_Nigar_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Running Scared (Eldar &amp; Nigar song)">Running Scared</a>", entitling Azerbaijan to host the contest in <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2012" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2012">2012</a>, in Baku.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> They have qualified for every Grand Final up until the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2018" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2018">2018 edition of the contest</a>, entering with <a href="/wiki/X_My_Heart_(song)" title="X My Heart (song)">X My Heart</a> by singer <a href="/wiki/Aisel_(singer)" title="Aisel (singer)">Aisel</a>
</p><p>There are dozens of Azerbaijani <a href="/wiki/Folk_dance" title="Folk dance">folk dances</a>. They are performed at formal celebrations and the dancers wear national clothes like the <a href="/wiki/Chokha" title="Chokha">Chokha</a>, which is well-preserved within the national dances. Most dances have a very fast rhythm. The national dance shows the characteristics of the Azerbaijani nation.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_literature" title="Azerbaijani literature">Azerbaijani literature</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Khurshidbanu_Natavan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Khurshidbanu_Natavan.jpg/180px-Khurshidbanu_Natavan.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Khurshidbanu_Natavan.jpg/270px-Khurshidbanu_Natavan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Khurshidbanu_Natavan.jpg/360px-Khurshidbanu_Natavan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2122" data-file-height="3289" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Khurshidbanu_Natavan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Painting of <a href="/wiki/Khurshidbanu_Natavan" title="Khurshidbanu Natavan">Khurshidbanu Natavan</a>, one of the most distinguished Azerbaijani poets. She was also the daughter of the last ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Karabakh_Khanate" title="Karabakh Khanate">Karabakh Khanate</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Among the medieval authors born within the territorial limits of modern Azerbaijani Republic was Persian poet and philosopher <a href="/wiki/Nizami_Ganjavi" title="Nizami Ganjavi">Nizami</a>, called Ganjavi after his place of birth, <a href="/wiki/Ganja,_Azerbaijan" title="Ganja, Azerbaijan">Ganja</a>, who was the author of the <a href="/wiki/Khamseh" title="Khamseh">Khamseh</a> ("The Quintuplet"), composed of five romantic poems, including "The Treasure of Mysteries," "Khosrow and Shīrīn," and "Leyli and Mejnūn."<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The earliest known figure in Azerbaijani literature was <a href="/wiki/Izzeddin_Hasanoglu" title="Izzeddin Hasanoglu">Izzeddin Hasanoglu</a>, who composed a <a href="/wiki/Diwan_(poetry)" title="Diwan (poetry)">divan</a> consisting of Persian and Turkic <a href="/wiki/Ghazal" title="Ghazal">ghazals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-beale_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beale-256">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-caferoglu_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caferoglu-257">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> In Persian ghazals he used his pen-name, while his Turkic ghazals were composed under his own name of Hasanoghlu.<sup id="cite_ref-beale_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beale-256">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Classical literature in Azerbaijani was formed in the 14th century based on the various Early Middle Ages dialects of <a href="/wiki/Tabriz" title="Tabriz">Tabriz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shirvan" title="Shirvan">Shirvan</a>. Among the poets of this period were <a href="/wiki/Kadi_Burhan_al-Din" title="Kadi Burhan al-Din">Gazi Burhanaddin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jahan_Shah" title="Jahan Shah">Haqiqi</a> (pen-name of <a href="/wiki/Jahan_Shah" title="Jahan Shah">Jahan-shah Qara Qoyunlu</a>), and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Habibi_(poet)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Habibi (poet) (page does not exist)">Habibi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tyrrell1_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tyrrell1-258">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> The end of the 14th century was also the period of starting literary activity of <a href="/wiki/Nesimi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nesimi">Imadaddin Nesimi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> one of the greatest <a href="/wiki/Turkic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkic language">Turkic</a><sup id="cite_ref-baldick_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baldick-260">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-burrill_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burrill-261">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cambridge_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge-262">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hurufi" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurufi">Hurufi</a> <a href="/wiki/Mysticism" title="Mysticism">mystical</a> poets of the late 14th and early 15th centuries<sup id="cite_ref-nesimibritannica_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nesimibritannica-263">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> and one of the most prominent early divan masters in Turkic literary history,<sup id="cite_ref-nesimibritannica_263-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nesimibritannica-263">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> who also composed poetry in <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a><sup id="cite_ref-burrill_261-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burrill-261">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-babinger_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-babinger-264">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nesimibritannica_263-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nesimibritannica-263">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> The divan and ghazal styles were further developed by poets <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qasim_al-Anvar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Qasim al-Anvar (page does not exist)">Qasim al-Anvar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuz%C3%BBl%C3%AE" title="Fuzûlî">Fuzuli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khatai" class="mw-redirect" title="Khatai">Khatai</a> (pen-name of <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid</a> <a href="/wiki/Shah_Ismail_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Shah Ismail I">Shah Ismail I</a>).
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Dede_Korkut" title="Book of Dede Korkut">Book of Dede Korkut</a> consists of two manuscripts copied in the 16th century,<sup id="cite_ref-Meeker_265-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meeker-265">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> was not written earlier than the 15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Kafadar_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kafadar-266">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IranicaOguzKhan_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IranicaOguzKhan-267">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> It is a collection of 12 stories reflecting the oral tradition of Oghuz nomads.<sup id="cite_ref-IranicaOguzKhan_267-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IranicaOguzKhan-267">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> The 16th-century poet, Muhammed Fuzuli produced his timeless philosophical and lyrical <i>Qazals</i> in Arabic, Persian, and Azerbaijani. Benefiting immensely from the fine literary traditions of his environment, and building upon the legacy of his predecessors, Fizuli was destined to become the leading literary figure of his society. His major works include <i>The Divan of Ghazals</i> and <i>The Qasidas</i>. In the same century, Azerbaijani literature further flourished with the development of <a href="/wiki/Ashik" title="Ashik">Ashik</a> (<a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>: <i lang="az">Aşıq</i>) poetic genre of bards. During the same period, under the pen-name of Khatāī (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">خطائی</span>&#8206; for <i>sinner</i>) Shah Ismail I wrote about 1400 verses in Azerbaijani,<sup id="cite_ref-minorsky1_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minorsky1-268">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> which were later published as his <i>Divan</i>. A unique literary style known as <i>qoshma</i> (<a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>: <i lang="az">qoşma</i> for <i>improvization</i>) was introduced in this period, and developed by Shah Ismail and later by his son and successor, Shah <a href="/wiki/Tahmasp_I" title="Tahmasp I">Tahmasp I</a>.
</p><p>In the span of the 17th and 18th centuries, Fizuli's unique genres as well <a href="/wiki/Ashik" title="Ashik">Ashik</a> poetry were taken up by prominent poets and writers such as <a href="/wiki/Qovsi_of_Tabriz" class="mw-redirect" title="Qovsi of Tabriz">Qovsi of Tabriz</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Abbas_II_of_Iran&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Abbas II of Iran (page does not exist)">Shah Abbas Sani</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Agha_Mesih_Shirvani&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Agha Mesih Shirvani (page does not exist)">Agha Mesih Shirvani</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nishat_(poet)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nishat (poet) (page does not exist)">Nishat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molla_Vali_Vidadi" title="Molla Vali Vidadi">Molla Vali Vidadi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Molla_Panah_Vagif" title="Molla Panah Vagif">Molla Panah Vagif</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Amani_(poet)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Amani (poet) (page does not exist)">Amani</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Zafar_(poet)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zafar (poet) (page does not exist)">Zafar</a> and others. Along with <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmens" title="Turkmens">Turkmens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijanis" title="Azerbaijanis">Azerbaijanis</a> also celebrate the <a href="/wiki/Epic_of_Koroglu" class="mw-redirect" title="Epic of Koroglu">Epic of Koroglu</a> (from <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_language" title="Azerbaijani language">Azerbaijani</a>: <i lang="az">kor oğlu</i> for <i>blind man's son</i>), a legendary folk hero.<sup id="cite_ref-samuel_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samuel-269">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> Several documented versions of Koroglu epic remain at the Institute for Manuscripts of the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences_of_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="National Academy of Sciences of Azerbaijan">National Academy of Sciences of Azerbaijan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-caferoglu_257-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-caferoglu-257">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Modern literature in Azerbaijan is based on the Shirvani dialect mainly, while in Iran it is based on the Tabrizi one. The first newspaper in Azerbaijani, <i><a href="/wiki/Akinchi" title="Akinchi">Akinchi</a></i> was published in 1875. In the mid-19th century, it was taught in the schools of <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ganja_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ganja (city)">Ganja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaki,_Azerbaijan" title="Shaki, Azerbaijan">Shaki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tbilisi" title="Tbilisi">Tbilisi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a>. Since 1845, it has also been taught in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Saint_Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Saint Petersburg">University of Saint Petersburg</a> in Russia.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Folk_art">Folk art</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_folk_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani folk art">Azerbaijani folk art</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbaijan_tradition.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Azerbaijan_tradition.jpg/150px-Azerbaijan_tradition.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Azerbaijan_tradition.jpg/225px-Azerbaijan_tradition.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Azerbaijan_tradition.jpg/300px-Azerbaijan_tradition.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1793" data-file-height="2689" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Azerbaijan_tradition.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional Azerbaijani clothing and musical instruments</div></div></div>
<p>Azerbaijanis have a rich and distinctive culture, a major part of which is <a href="/wiki/Decorative_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Decorative art">decorative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Applied_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Applied art">applied art</a>. This form of art is represented by a wide range of handicrafts, such as chasing, jeweler, engraving in metal, carving in wood, stone and bone, carpet-making, lasing, pattern weaving and printing, knitting and embroidery. Each of these types of decorative art, evidence of the endowments of the Azerbaijan nation, is very much in favor here. Many interesting facts pertaining to the development of arts and crafts in Azerbaijan were reported by numerous merchants, travelers and diplomats who had visited these places at different times.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_rug" title="Azerbaijani rug">Azerbaijani carpet</a> is a traditional handmade textile of various sizes, with dense texture and a pile or pile-less surface, whose patterns are characteristic of Azerbaijan's many carpet-making regions. In November 2010 the Azerbaijani carpet was proclaimed a <a href="/wiki/Masterpieces_of_the_Oral_and_Intangible_Heritage_of_Humanity" title="Masterpieces of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity">Masterpiece of Intangible Heritage</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lahic_folk_art.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Lahic_folk_art.png/220px-Lahic_folk_art.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Lahic_folk_art.png/330px-Lahic_folk_art.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Lahic_folk_art.png/440px-Lahic_folk_art.png 2x" data-file-width="4372" data-file-height="2906" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lahic_folk_art.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Handwork coppery in <a href="/wiki/Lah%C4%B1c,_Ismailli" title="Lahıc, Ismailli">Lahic</a></div></div></div>
<p>Azerbaijan has been since the ancient times known as a center of a large variety of crafts. The archeological dig on the territory of Azerbaijan testifies to the well developed agriculture, stock raising, metal working, pottery, ceramics, and carpet-weaving that date as far back as to the 2nd millennium BC. Archeological sites in Dashbulaq, Hasansu, Zayamchai, and Tovuzchai uncovered from the BTC pipeline have revealed early Iron Age artifacts.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Azerbaijani carpets can be categorized under several large groups and a multitude of subgroups. Scientific research of the Azerbaijani carpet is connected with the name of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latif_Kerimov&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Latif Kerimov (page does not exist)">Latif Kerimov</a>, a prominent scientist and artist. It was his classification that related the four large groups of carpets with the four geographical zones of Azerbaijan, Guba-Shirvan, Ganja-Kazakh, Karabakh and Tabriz.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_cuisine" title="Azerbaijani cuisine">Azerbaijani cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dushbara_Azerbaijani_cuisine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Dushbara_Azerbaijani_cuisine.jpg/150px-Dushbara_Azerbaijani_cuisine.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Dushbara_Azerbaijani_cuisine.jpg/225px-Dushbara_Azerbaijani_cuisine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Dushbara_Azerbaijani_cuisine.jpg/300px-Dushbara_Azerbaijani_cuisine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1811" data-file-height="1592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dushbara_Azerbaijani_cuisine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dushbara" class="mw-redirect" title="Dushbara">Dushbara</a>, a traditional Azerbaijani meal</div></div></div>
<p>The traditional cuisine is famous for an abundance of vegetables and greens used seasonally in the dishes. Fresh herbs, including mint, cilantro (coriander), dill, basil, parsley, tarragon, leeks, chives, thyme, marjoram, green onion, and watercress, are very popular and often accompany main dishes on the table. Climatic diversity and fertility of the land are reflected in the national dishes, which are based on fish from the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>, local meat (mainly mutton and beef), and an abundance of seasonal vegetables and greens. Saffron-rice <a href="/wiki/Plov" class="mw-redirect" title="Plov">plov</a> is the flagship food in Azerbaijan and <a href="/wiki/Black_tea" title="Black tea">black tea</a> is the national beverage.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijanis often use traditional <a href="/wiki/Armudu" title="Armudu">armudu</a> (pear-shaped) glass as they have very strong <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_tea_culture" title="Azerbaijani tea culture">tea culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aze_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aze-275">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> Popular traditional dishes include <i>bozbash</i> (lamb soup that exists in several regional varieties with the addition of different vegetables), <a href="/wiki/Qutab" title="Qutab">qutab</a> (fried turnover with a filling of greens or minced meat) and <a href="/wiki/Dushbara" class="mw-redirect" title="Dushbara">dushbara</a> (sort of dumplings of dough filled with ground meat and flavor).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Azerbaijan" title="Architecture of Azerbaijan">Architecture of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Momine_Hatoon_Mausoleum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Momine_Hatoon_Mausoleum.jpg/220px-Momine_Hatoon_Mausoleum.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Momine_Hatoon_Mausoleum.jpg/330px-Momine_Hatoon_Mausoleum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Momine_Hatoon_Mausoleum.jpg/440px-Momine_Hatoon_Mausoleum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1270" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Momine_Hatoon_Mausoleum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Momine_Khatun_Mausoleum" title="Momine Khatun Mausoleum">Momine Khatun Mausoleum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nakhchivan_(city)" title="Nakhchivan (city)">Nakhchivan</a> built in the 12th century</div></div></div>
<p>Azerbaijani architecture typically combines elements of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">West</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijiani architecture has heavy influences from Persian architecture. Many ancient architectural treasures such as the <a href="/wiki/Maiden_Tower_(Baku)" title="Maiden Tower (Baku)">Maiden Tower</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Shirvanshahs" title="Palace of the Shirvanshahs">Palace of the Shirvanshahs</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Walled City of Baku</a> survive in modern Azerbaijan. Entries submitted on the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage">UNESCO World Heritage</a> tentative list include the <a href="/wiki/Ateshgah_of_Baku" title="Ateshgah of Baku">Ateshgah of Baku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Momine_Khatun_Mausoleum" title="Momine Khatun Mausoleum">Momine Khatun Mausoleum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hirkan_National_Park" title="Hirkan National Park">Hirkan National Park</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Binegadi_National_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Binegadi National Park (page does not exist)">Binegadi National Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/L%C3%B6kbatan_Mud_Volcano" title="Lökbatan Mud Volcano">Lökbatan Mud Volcano</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baku_Stage_Mountain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Baku Stage Mountain (page does not exist)">Baku Stage Mountain</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Caspian_Shore_Defensive_Constructions&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Caspian Shore Defensive Constructions (page does not exist)">Caspian Shore Defensive Constructions</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Shusha_National_Reserve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Shusha National Reserve (page does not exist)">Shusha National Reserve</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ordubad_National_Reserve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ordubad National Reserve (page does not exist)">Ordubad National Reserve</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Shaki_Khans" title="Palace of Shaki Khans">Palace of Shaki Khans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Among other architectural treasures are <a href="/wiki/Quadrangular_castle_(Mardakan)" title="Quadrangular castle (Mardakan)">Quadrangular Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mardakan" class="mw-redirect" title="Mardakan">Mardakan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parigala" title="Parigala">Parigala</a> in <a href="/wiki/Yuxar%C4%B1_%C3%87ardaqlar" title="Yuxarı Çardaqlar">Yukhary Chardaglar</a>, a number of bridges spanning the Aras River, and several mausoleums. In the 19th and early 20th centuries, little monumental architecture was created, but distinctive residences were built in Baku and elsewhere. Among the most recent architectural monuments, the <a href="/wiki/Baku_Metro" title="Baku Metro">Baku subways</a> are noted for their lavish decor.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The task for modern Azerbaijani architecture is diverse application of modern aesthetics, the search for an architect's own artistic style and inclusion of the existing historico-cultural environment. Major projects such as <a href="/wiki/Heydar_Aliyev_Cultural_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Heydar Aliyev Cultural Center">Heydar Aliyev Cultural Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Flame_Towers" title="Flame Towers">Flame Towers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baku_Crystal_Hall" title="Baku Crystal Hall">Baku Crystal Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baku_White_City" title="Baku White City">Baku White City</a> and <a href="/wiki/SOCAR_Tower" title="SOCAR Tower">SOCAR Tower</a> have transformed the country's skyline and promotes its contemporary identity.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_art">Visual art</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Visual_arts_of_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Visual arts of Azerbaijan">Visual arts of Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheki_dvoretc_rospisi_az.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Sheki_dvoretc_rospisi_az.jpg/400px-Sheki_dvoretc_rospisi_az.jpg" decoding="async" width="400" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Sheki_dvoretc_rospisi_az.jpg/600px-Sheki_dvoretc_rospisi_az.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8b/Sheki_dvoretc_rospisi_az.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="337" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheki_dvoretc_rospisi_az.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Miniature_(illuminated_manuscript)" title="Miniature (illuminated manuscript)">miniature painting</a> of a battle scene on the walls of the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Shaki_Khans" title="Palace of Shaki Khans">Palace of Shaki Khans</a>, 18th century, <a href="/wiki/Shaki,_Azerbaijan" title="Shaki, Azerbaijan">city of Shaki</a></div></div></div>
<p>Azerbaijani art includes one of the oldest art objects in the world, which were discovered as <a href="/wiki/Gamigaya_Petroglyphs" title="Gamigaya Petroglyphs">Gamigaya Petroglyphs</a> in the territory of <a href="/wiki/Ordubad_Rayon" class="mw-redirect" title="Ordubad Rayon">Ordubad Rayon</a> are dated back to the 1st to 4th centuries BC. About 1500 dislodged and carved rock paintings with images of deer, goats, bulls, dogs, snakes, birds, fantastic beings and also people, carriages and various symbols had been found out on basalt rocks.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Ethnographer" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnographer">ethnographer</a> and adventurer <a href="/wiki/Thor_Heyerdahl" title="Thor Heyerdahl">Thor Heyerdahl</a> was convinced that people from the area went to <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a> in about 100 AD, took their boat building skills with them, and transmuted them into the Viking boats in Northern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over the centuries, Azerbaijani art has gone through many stylistic changes. Azerbaijani painting is traditionally characterized by a warmth of colour and light, as exemplified in the works of <a href="/wiki/Azim_Azimzade" title="Azim Azimzade">Azim Azimzade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bahruz_Kangarli" title="Bahruz Kangarli">Bahruz Kangarli</a>, and a preoccupation with religious figures and cultural motifs.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijani painting enjoyed preeminence in Caucasus for hundreds of years, from the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_art" title="Romanesque art">Romanesque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Culture of the Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> periods, and through the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_realism" title="Socialist realism">Soviet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> periods, the latter two of which saw fruition in Azerbaijan. Other notable artists who fall within these periods include <a href="/wiki/Sattar_Bahlulzade" title="Sattar Bahlulzade">Sattar Bahlulzade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Togrul_Narimanbekov" title="Togrul Narimanbekov">Togrul Narimanbekov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tahir_Salahov" title="Tahir Salahov">Tahir Salahov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alakbar_Rezaguliyev" title="Alakbar Rezaguliyev">Alakbar Rezaguliyev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mirza_Gadim_Iravani" class="mw-redirect" title="Mirza Gadim Iravani">Mirza Gadim Iravani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mikayil_Abdullayev" title="Mikayil Abdullayev">Mikayil Abdullayev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boyukagha_Mirzazade" title="Boyukagha Mirzazade">Boyukagha Mirzazade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<center>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional" style="max-width: 1106px;_width: 1106px;">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 150px"><div style="width: 150px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Film_of_Azerbaijan_1916.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Film_of_Azerbaijan_1916.jpg/220px-Film_of_Azerbaijan_1916.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Film_of_Azerbaijan_1916.jpg/330px-Film_of_Azerbaijan_1916.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Film_of_Azerbaijan_1916.jpg/440px-Film_of_Azerbaijan_1916.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="489" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Film_of_Azerbaijan_1916.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Scene from the Azerbaijani film <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Kingdom_of_Oil_and_Millions" title="In the Kingdom of Oil and Millions">In the Kingdom of Oil and Millions</a></i>, 1916</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Azerbaijan" title="Cinema of Azerbaijan">Cinema of Azerbaijan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_animation" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani animation">Azerbaijani animation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Azerbaijan" title="Television in Azerbaijan">Television in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<p>The film industry in Azerbaijan dates back to 1898. In fact, Azerbaijan was among the first countries involved in <a href="/wiki/Cinematography" title="Cinematography">cinematography</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mishon_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mishon-289">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Therefore, it's not surprising that this apparatus soon showed up in <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> – at the start of the 20th century, this bay town on the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian</a> was producing more than 50 percent of the world's supply of oil. Just like today, the oil industry attracted foreigners eager to invest and to work.<sup id="cite_ref-cinemainazerbaijan_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cinemainazerbaijan-290">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> In 1919, during the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a>, a documentary <i>The Celebration of the Anniversary of Azerbaijani Independence</i> was filmed on the first anniversary of Azerbaijan's independence from Russia, 27 May, and premiered in June 1919 at several theatres in Baku.<sup id="cite_ref-ocaz_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocaz-291">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> After the Soviet power was established in 1920, Nariman Narimanov, Chairman of the Revolutionary Committee of Azerbaijan, signed a decree nationalizing Azerbaijan's cinema. This also influenced the creation of <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijani_animation" class="mw-redirect" title="Azerbaijani animation">Azerbaijani animation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ocaz_291-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ocaz-291">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1991, after Azerbaijan gained its independence from the Soviet Union, the first Baku International Film Festival East-West was held in Baku. In December 2000, the former President of Azerbaijan, Heydar Aliyev, signed a decree proclaiming 2 August to be the professional holiday of filmmakers of Azerbaijan. Today Azerbaijani filmmakers are again dealing with issues similar to those faced by cinematographers prior to the establishment of the Soviet Union in 1920. Once again, both choice of content and sponsorship of films are largely left up to the initiative of the filmmaker.<sup id="cite_ref-mishon_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mishon-289">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_media_freedom">Media and media freedom</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Azerbaijan" title="Media of Azerbaijan">Media of Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Media_freedom_in_Azerbaijan" title="Media freedom in Azerbaijan">Media freedom in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<p>There are three state-owned television channels: <a href="/wiki/AzTV" title="AzTV">AzTV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idman_Azerbaijan_TV" title="Idman Azerbaijan TV">Idman TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medeniyyet_TV" title="Medeniyyet TV">Medeniyyet TV</a>. One public channel and 6 private channels: <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0ctimai_Television" title="İctimai Television">İctimai Television</a>, <a href="/wiki/ANS_TV" title="ANS TV">ANS TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Space_TV" title="Space TV">Space TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lider_TV" title="Lider TV">Lider TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azad_Azerbaijan_TV" title="Azad Azerbaijan TV">Azad Azerbaijan TV</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Xazar_TV&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Xazar TV (page does not exist)">Xazar TV</a> and <a href="/wiki/Region_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Region TV">Region TV</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights_in_Azerbaijan">Human rights in Azerbaijan</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Azerbaijan" title="Human rights in Azerbaijan">Human rights in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rashadat_Akhundov.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Rashadat_Akhundov.jpg/220px-Rashadat_Akhundov.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Rashadat_Akhundov.jpg/330px-Rashadat_Akhundov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Rashadat_Akhundov.jpg/440px-Rashadat_Akhundov.jpg 2x" data-file-width="987" data-file-height="555" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rashadat_Akhundov.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rashadat_Akhundov" title="Rashadat Akhundov">Rashadat Akhundov</a>, the co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Nida_Civic_Movement" title="Nida Civic Movement">Nida Civic Movement</a>, was sentenced to 8 years of imprisonment on 6 May 2014.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Azerbaijan" title="Constitution of Azerbaijan">Constitution of Azerbaijan</a> claims to guarantee freedom of speech, but this is denied in practice. After several years of decline in press and media freedom, in 2014, the media environment in Azerbaijan deteriorated rapidly under a governmental campaign to silence any opposition and criticism, even while the country led the Committee of Ministers of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> (May–November 2014). Spurious legal charges and impunity in violence against journalists have remained the norm.<sup id="cite_ref-pace_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pace-292">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> All foreign broadcasts are banned in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FH_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH-293">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_Press_(report)" title="Freedom of the Press (report)">Freedom of the Press report</a>, Azerbaijan's press freedom status is "not free," and Azerbaijan ranks 177th out of 196 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty" title="Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty">Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">Voice of America</a> are banned in Azerbaijan.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> Discrimination against <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Azerbaijan" title="LGBT rights in Azerbaijan">LGBT people</a> in Azerbaijan is widespread.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the last few years,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (December 2017)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> three journalists were killed and several prosecuted in trials described as unfair by international human rights organizations. Azerbaijan had the biggest number of journalists imprisoned in Europe and Central Asia in 2015, according to the <a href="/wiki/Committee_to_Protect_Journalists" title="Committee to Protect Journalists">Committee to Protect Journalists</a>, and is the 5th most censored country in the world, ahead of Iran and China.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A report by an <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> researcher in October 2015 points to '...the severe deterioration of human rights in Azerbaijan over the past few years. Sadly Azerbaijan has been allowed to get away with unprecedented levels of repression and in the process almost wipe out its civil society'.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> Amnesty's 2015/16 annual report<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> on the country stated ' ... persecution of political dissent continued. Human rights organizations remained unable to resume their work. At least 18 prisoners of conscience remained in detention at the end of the year. Reprisals against independent journalists and activists persisted both in the country and abroad, while their family members also faced harassment and arrests. International human rights monitors were barred and expelled from the country. Reports of torture and other ill-treatment persisted.'
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> reported in April 2017 that "Azerbaijan's ruling elite operated a secret $2.9bn (£2.2bn) scheme to pay prominent Europeans, buy luxury goods and launder money through a network of opaque British companies .... Leaked data shows that the Azerbaijani leadership, accused of serial human rights abuses, systemic corruption and rigging elections, made more than 16,000 covert payments from 2012 to 2014. Some of this money went to politicians and journalists, as part of an international lobbying operation to deflect criticism of Azerbaijan's president, Ilham Aliyev, and to promote a positive image of his oil-rich country." There was no suggestion that all recipients were aware of the source of the money as it arrived via a disguised route.<sup id="cite_ref-Gdn4917_301-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gdn4917-301">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Azerbaijan" title="Sport in Azerbaijan">Sport in Azerbaijan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mamedyarov,_Shamkir_2016.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Mamedyarov%2C_Shamkir_2016.JPG/180px-Mamedyarov%2C_Shamkir_2016.JPG" decoding="async" width="180" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f1/Mamedyarov%2C_Shamkir_2016.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="266" data-file-height="400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mamedyarov,_Shamkir_2016.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Shakhriyar_Mamedyarov" title="Shakhriyar Mamedyarov">Shakhriyar Mamedyarov</a> was the 2013 <a href="/wiki/World_Rapid_Chess_Championship" title="World Rapid Chess Championship">World Rapid Chess</a> and three-time <a href="/wiki/European_Team_Chess_Championship" title="European Team Chess Championship">European Team Chess</a> champion.</div></div></div>
<p>Freestyle wrestling has been traditionally regarded as Azerbaijan's <a href="/wiki/National_sport" title="National sport">national sport</a>, in which Azerbaijan won up to <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_at_the_Olympics" title="Azerbaijan at the Olympics">fourteen medals</a>, including four golds since joining the <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committee</a>. Currently, the most popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> and wrestling.
</p><p>Football is the most popular sport in Azerbaijan, and the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Football_Federations_of_Azerbaijan" title="Association of Football Federations of Azerbaijan">Association of Football Federations of Azerbaijan</a> with 9,122 registered players, is the largest sporting association in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_national_football_team" title="Azerbaijan national football team">national football team</a> of Azerbaijan demonstrates relatively low performance in the international arena compared to the nation football clubs. The most successful Azerbaijani football clubs are <a href="/wiki/Neftchi_Baku_PFC" class="mw-redirect" title="Neftchi Baku PFC">Neftchi Baku</a>, <a href="/wiki/FK_Qaraba%C4%9F" class="mw-redirect" title="FK Qarabağ">Qarabağ</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gabala_FK" title="Gabala FK">Gabala</a>. In <a href="/wiki/2012-13_UEFA_Europa_League" class="mw-redirect" title="2012-13 UEFA Europa League">2012</a>, Neftchi Baku became the first Azerbaijani team to advance to the group stage of a European competition, beating <a href="/wiki/APOEL_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="APOEL F.C.">APOEL</a> of Cyprus 4–2 on aggregate in the play-off round of the <a href="/wiki/2012-13_UEFA_Europa_League" class="mw-redirect" title="2012-13 UEFA Europa League">2012-13 UEFA Europa League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/2014-15_UEFA_Europa_League" class="mw-redirect" title="2014-15 UEFA Europa League">2014</a>, Qarabağ became the second Azerbaijani club advancing to the group stage of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a>. In 2017, after beating <a href="/wiki/F.C._Copenhagen" title="F.C. Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> 2–2(<a href="/wiki/Away_goals_rule" title="Away goals rule">a</a>) in the play-off round of the <a href="/wiki/2017-18_UEFA_Champions_League" class="mw-redirect" title="2017-18 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>, Qarabağ became the first Azerbaijani club to reach the Group stage.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">Futsal</a> is another popular sport in Azerbaijan. The <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_national_futsal_team" title="Azerbaijan national futsal team">Azerbaijan national futsal team</a> reached fourth place in the <a href="/wiki/2010_UEFA_Futsal_Championship" title="2010 UEFA Futsal Championship">2010 UEFA Futsal Championship</a>, while domestic club <a href="/wiki/Araz_Nax%C3%A7ivan" title="Araz Naxçivan">Araz Naxçivan</a> clinched bronze medals at the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_UEFA_Futsal_Cup" title="2009–10 UEFA Futsal Cup">2009–10 UEFA Futsal Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Futsal_Cup" title="2013–14 UEFA Futsal Cup">2013–14 UEFA Futsal Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijan was the main sponsor of Spanish football club <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_de_Madrid" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlético de Madrid">Atlético de Madrid</a> during seasons 2013/2014 and 2014/2015, a partnership that the club described should 'promote the image of Azerbaijan in the world'.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Backgammon" title="Backgammon">Backgammon</a> also plays a major role in Azerbaijani culture.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> The game is very popular in Azerbaijan and is widely played among the local public.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> There are also different variations of backgammon developed and analyzed by Azerbaijani experts.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_opening_ceremony_of_the_first_European_games_7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/The_opening_ceremony_of_the_first_European_games_7.jpg/220px-The_opening_ceremony_of_the_first_European_games_7.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/The_opening_ceremony_of_the_first_European_games_7.jpg/330px-The_opening_ceremony_of_the_first_European_games_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/The_opening_ceremony_of_the_first_European_games_7.jpg/440px-The_opening_ceremony_of_the_first_European_games_7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_opening_ceremony_of_the_first_European_games_7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Baku_National_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Baku National Stadium">Baku National Stadium</a> was used for the first <a href="/wiki/European_Games" title="European Games">European Games</a> in June 2015.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Women%27s_Volleyball_Super_League" title="Azerbaijan Women&#39;s Volleyball Super League">Azerbaijan Women's Volleyball Super League</a> is one of strongest women leagues in world. Its women's national team came fourth at the <a href="/wiki/2005_Women%27s_European_Volleyball_Championship" title="2005 Women&#39;s European Volleyball Championship">2005 European Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> Over the last years, clubs like <a href="/wiki/Rabita_Baku" class="mw-redirect" title="Rabita Baku">Rabita Baku</a> and <a href="/wiki/Azerrail_Baku" title="Azerrail Baku">Azerrail Baku</a> achieved great success at European cups.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> Azerbaijani volleyball players include likes of <a href="/wiki/Valeriya_Korotenko" class="mw-redirect" title="Valeriya Korotenko">Valeriya Korotenko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oksana_Parkhomenko" class="mw-redirect" title="Oksana Parkhomenko">Oksana Parkhomenko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inessa_Korkmaz" title="Inessa Korkmaz">Inessa Korkmaz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natalya_Mammadova" title="Natalya Mammadova">Natalya Mammadova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alla_Hasanova" title="Alla Hasanova">Alla Hasanova</a>.
</p><p>Other well-known Azerbaijani athletes are <a href="/wiki/Namig_Abdullayev" title="Namig Abdullayev">Namig Abdullayev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toghrul_Asgarov" title="Toghrul Asgarov">Toghrul Asgarov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rovshan_Bayramov" title="Rovshan Bayramov">Rovshan Bayramov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sharif_Sharifov" title="Sharif Sharifov">Sharif Sharifov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariya_Stadnik" title="Mariya Stadnik">Mariya Stadnik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Farid_Mansurov" title="Farid Mansurov">Farid Mansurov</a> in <a href="/wiki/Amateur_wrestling" title="Amateur wrestling">wrestling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nazim_Huseynov" title="Nazim Huseynov">Nazim Huseynov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elnur_Mammadli" title="Elnur Mammadli">Elnur Mammadli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elkhan_Mammadov_(judoka)" title="Elkhan Mammadov (judoka)">Elkhan Mammadov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rustam_Orujov" title="Rustam Orujov">Rustam Orujov</a> in judo, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Aghayev" title="Rafael Aghayev">Rafael Aghayev</a> in <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magomedrasul_Majidov" title="Magomedrasul Majidov">Magomedrasul Majidov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aghasi_Mammadov" title="Aghasi Mammadov">Aghasi Mammadov</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nizami_Pashayev" title="Nizami Pashayev">Nizami Pashayev</a> in <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">Olympic weightlifting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azad_Asgarov" title="Azad Asgarov">Azad Asgarov</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pankration" title="Pankration">pankration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Mammadov" title="Eduard Mammadov">Eduard Mammadov</a> in kickboxing, and <a href="/wiki/K-1" title="K-1">K-1</a> fighter <a href="/wiki/Zabit_Samedov" title="Zabit Samedov">Zabit Samedov</a>.
</p><p>Azerbaijan has a <a href="/wiki/Baku_City_Circuit" title="Baku City Circuit">Formula One race-track</a>, made in June 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> and the country hosted its first <a href="/wiki/2016_European_Grand_Prix" title="2016 European Grand Prix">Formula One Grand Prix</a> on 19 June 2016<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Grand_Prix" title="Azerbaijan Grand Prix">Azerbaijan Grand Prix</a> in 2017, 2018 and 2019. Other annual sporting events held in the country are the <a href="/wiki/Baku_Cup" title="Baku Cup">Baku Cup</a> tennis tournament and the <a href="/wiki/Tour_d%27Azerba%C3%AFdjan" title="Tour d&#39;Azerbaïdjan">Tour d'Azerbaïdjan</a> cycling race.
</p><p>Azerbaijan hosted several major sport competitions since the late 2000s, including the <a href="/wiki/2013_F1_Powerboat_World_Championship_season" class="mw-redirect" title="2013 F1 Powerboat World Championship season">2013 F1 Powerboat World Championship</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_FIFA_U-17_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2012 FIFA U-17 Women&#39;s World Cup">2012 FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011_AIBA_World_Boxing_Championships" title="2011 AIBA World Boxing Championships">2011 AIBA World Boxing Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_European_Wrestling_Championships" title="2010 European Wrestling Championships">2010 European Wrestling Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_Rhythmic_Gymnastics_European_Championships" title="2009 Rhythmic Gymnastics European Championships">2009 Rhythmic Gymnastics European Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Taekwondo_Championships" title="European Taekwondo Championships">2014 European Taekwondo Championships</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_Rhythmic_Gymnastics_European_Championships" title="2014 Rhythmic Gymnastics European Championships">2014 Rhythmic Gymnastics European Championships</a>, and <a href="/wiki/42nd_Chess_Olympiad" title="42nd Chess Olympiad">2016 World Chess Olympiad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> On 8 December 2012, <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> was selected to host the <a href="/wiki/2015_European_Games" title="2015 European Games">2015 European Games</a>, the first to be held in the competition's history.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> Baku is also set to host the fourth <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Solidarity_Games" title="Islamic Solidarity Games">Islamic Solidarity Games</a> in 2017 And <a href="/wiki/2019_European_Youth_Summer_Olympic_Festival" title="2019 European Youth Summer Olympic Festival">2019 European Youth Summer Olympic Festival</a> in 2019 And also One of the hosts of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">UEFA Euro 2020</a>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

London: <a href="/wiki/Palgrave_Macmillan" title="Palgrave Macmillan">Palgrave Macmillan</a> (published 15 May 2016). pp.&#160;91–117. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1057%2F978-1-137-38781-3_4">10.1057/978-1-137-38781-3_4</a>. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-137-38780-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-137-38780-6"><bdi>978-1-137-38780-6</bdi></a>. <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress_Control_Number" title="Library of Congress Control Number">LCCN</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//lccn.loc.gov/2016939393">2016939393</a>. <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">OCLC</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/6039791976">6039791976</a>. <q>LaPorte examines the dynamics of semi-presidentialism in Azerbaijan. Azerbaijan's regime is a curious hybrid, in which semi-presidential institutions operate in the larger context of authoritarianism. The author compares formal Constitutional provisions with the practice of politics in the country, suggesting that formal and informal sources of authority come together to enhance the effective powers of the presidency. In addition to the considerable formal powers laid out in the Constitution, Azerbaijan's president also benefits from the support of the ruling party and informal family and patronage networks. LaPorte concludes by discussing the theoretical implications of this symbiosis between formal and informal institutions in Azerbaijan's semi-presidential regime.</q></cite><span
